de albaras	The use of cautery to address swelling in specific areas necessitates careful application based on the affected limb's dimensions; a slight penetration into the skin is advised for visibility. Subsequent treatment should include ointments until healing occurs. Additionally, cautery has been applied to extremities and spine locations associated with nerve function that can lead to bone deformity when not properly managed; however, intervention in such cases should be avoided unless the practitioner is knowledgeable about muscle functions and neurovascular pathways within the body.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color;	 When the disease called "albaras" is old, and medical methods are of no use, then cauterize with a caustic agent slightly by its edge, according to the amount determined by the severity, until the discoloration is removed, and it changes color.
puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie;	 then apply a poultice of flour and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood from the colt's leg and crane bird (swan), one part each.
et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then mix all together, bind with a cloth, and place hot stones underneath until it is properly healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of ulcers by fire cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	 When a sore begins to appear and you can see it, cauterize with the cautery that appears as a circle all around the sore.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre;	 And yet the wise say to do cautery as well with millet poultices for cankers.
et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois;	 And yet it does not seem good to me, as I have found them often becoming ulcerated and corrupted.
et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	 And more appropriate it is that they be cauterized around the "circulating" cautery, as we have said in many treatises on cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	Of the inflammation that cannot die out
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens;	 When some have a disease called "adubelati", and it delays dying either due to excessive secretion or the state of the patient being weakened (that is, too old) with little blood.
et tu la vues haster de meurer:	 and you observe them hastening to die:
adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant;	 Then you must cauterize around with many small cauteries by pricking.
aprés le laisse ensi.	 After this, let it be as such.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	 For she will delay dying.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierced throughout the cautery, heat the cautery of which there is a shape:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	 And place your hand in the midst of that illness called "adubeati" until it feels like burns, and let the caustic burns be such that the patient senses them behind as if following the course of inflammation.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 After the treatment until it is completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The healing of fire with iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	 Another manner of disease called "corrodens," which is nothing but a mixture affecting the limbs, as it consumes them like dry branches are consumed by fire.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est;	 If you see this disease in place that can suffer a burning together with fire, then fan the small and large cauldrons as much as needed depending on where the body or illness is located.
aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	 After you have burned all parts until you remove the entire corruption, and nothing remains of it, let everything that is corrupted be consumed by fire.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	 And then let it rest for three days and apply wet compressions with oil until the burns from fire have healed, and all corruption is gone.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	 After applying oil treatments that produce heat.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin;	 And if after three days no wound heals, this is good;
et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	 and if not, resume the burning on that which remains from the corrupted parts.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu;	 This mixture has sometimes been treated with cold water as a fire cautery.
mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division:	 But always, the fire cautery is of greater help; and I have already described the treatment with cold water in its application.
pren la quant tu en as mestier.	 Take the quantity that you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	Of pus that comes to the joints.
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	 Often in the feet there arises a disease which we call "clot" and it is a significant swelling that presses on the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	 And the fire treatment for this disease is as follows: two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	 It is known as fire cautery, and water cautery hot.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges;	 The fire cautery is one that you heat like a penny on a hearth, and it should be made of good iron to pierce through the nail in all directions, and have fine edges.
aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou;	 After heating it thoroughly on the nail, turn your hand completely around the nail until it becomes red with heat.
et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture;	 and let it remain like this for three days until it begins to produce pus.
puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	 Then make an emplaster of well-ground henbane mixed with wax, and leave the plaster on throughout the night, and it will draw out and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then treat the limb with soothing ointment until it is healed cleanly.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude;	 And if they are infected towards the rear of the body, and it happens many times in hands and feet, then you must treat with a hot water cauterization.
et est en teil maniere:	 and occurs in such a manner:
pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues;	 take a needle of copper or iron, or a spatula of silver, and place it on the splinter and the flesh underneath, that is to say for removing warts.
et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine;	 and insert the needle so that it perforates all around, then place some hot water on it, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand as you rotate until the edge of the needle reaches to the root of the splinter, allowing the hot water to penetrate deeply up to the root.
et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre;	 And the patient suffers a little from the sting of warm water for an hour.
puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	 Then let it be so, and it will uproot all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	 So do another after the other, touching all that are on the body, then treat them with ointments containing wax.
li cure dou trembler	them on; This is not to: est untines a la chauges until the be it. The time that tand rele your de ouga:
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee;	 When some suffer from shivers due to coldness or fever quaternary (fourth degree) or another type, it is necessary for you to perform four cauterizations above the spine of the back, one between each vertebra.
et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire;	 and one on the navel with an olive cautery;
si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	 if this will make them shake, and it shall rid them of the illness' cold sickness.
des pustules puans	Of pus-filled sores
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	 In no case become apparent from behind in bodies bathed or pus-filled, which come from large corrupted substances.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule:	 if at first they appear that a cautery is made upon each head of the pustule:;
un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	 A subtle cautery made of poplar wood, so that the tip is gripped by fire, or from a long yew root, or on a lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez;	 And never should you cauterize at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow any further forward, but it breaks off the excess that comes from them, leaving clean.
mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	 But it is necessary that this be done after blood evacuation.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses;	 Often great harm to the artery occurs when it is cut at the wound edge, or during an abscess incision, or on limb cauterization, and similar things.
et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	 And this is a very serious thing to stop bleeding.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus;	 And yet when this happens to anyone, quickly place your index finger on the wound of the vein, and strain very much until the blood ceases below your finger, and it no longer flows out.
puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge;	 Then apply fire to olive wood cauldrons of various sizes until they are all red-hot.
puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	 Then take one large or small according to the wound and its location where the artery is located, place the cauldery over that vein while holding your finger in place, and hold the cauldron until the blood is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	When it bursts out as you lift your elbow over the vein, and the cautery is spent, then quickly take another of the cauteries which are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez;	 And continue doing so one after another until the bleeding has ceased.
et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide;	 And be cautious not to burn the nerve near it and that no other harm comes upon the patient.
et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit:	 And you say that when the artery is cut short, it cannot be properly tied up on its own, especially if the artery is large, unless by one of the four methods we have mentioned.
ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc;	 Or through cauterization, or through extracting when it cannot be treated well, or by strongly binding with thread, or by applying medicines that have the power to stop bleeding.
et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	 And is tied and strained temporarily.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will perform the proper closing of straining tightly with cloth or applying burning substances above, or similar things; if it does not benefit greatly.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne;	 And if it happens to anyone who has no remedy or medicine at hand, then they should place their thumb index over the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch out well until bleeding is stopped above the wound and above the vein.
et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez;	 And he must not move it, but keep the cold wet cloth on it often as needed until the blood is congealed and thickened.
et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	 Then make incisions forward as required for cauterization and application of medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of wound treatment methods.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres;	 We have told you in the first chapter about all illnesses that require fire cauterization or burning medicines, and blisters, pus, efflorescence, and the appearance of burn marks.
et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	 And I have included that chapter on the head up to the temples, and I will go through this chapter by the same method for what is found more easily therein.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so as I begin this section, it is necessary for you to learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than the first of cauteries, hence greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses;	 For in the work of this chapter, there is often evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incision into an abscess, and wound treatments, and arrow extractions, and incision for stones, and similar things.
ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	 When there is doubt and fear, death comes to many others.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	 And I warn you to not undertake folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	 For there are many ways that people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice;	 If they come from those who have suffered so much with their illness that they die easily due to the severity of their disease and its magnitude.
et de ces doit on avoir paor.	 And one must fear such things.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit:	 And there are some who lose their mind, saying:
«atendez, je sui garis»;	 "Wait, I am healed;
et li maladie est despitouse.	 and the illness is defiant.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los;	 You should not easily give in to those who approach you with this behavior, but show greater compassion than greed, and do not hastily undertake what you are sure of and have confidently accepted.
et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie;	 And make use of prediction and guidance for directing treatments to your patients so that health may be restored.
et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	 And this will assist you in gaining good reputation, glory, and the memory of the Lord.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dearest son of our lords, Our Lord grants you good understanding and rectitude, and if you wish to aspire from the holy inspiration of His hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered this treatise by chapters as seen in the chapter of cauteries that I have explained from head to toe, so that you may find it easier to understand what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	Full of water within the head
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant;	 Know that this illness often occurs in children during birth, and when the child's head is pulled too hard.
et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	 At no time does this result occur if one knows how to reset it properly.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors;	 And I have never seen this disease outside of children, and all those I have seen succumb quickly.
et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	 and therefore it seems to me that one should not attempt healing in these cases.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir;	 And I saw a child whose head was filled with water, and the skull grew each day until it could no longer bear.
et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os;	 and believed so much in the water that they died, and this swelling is accumulated under the bone above the suture between the skin and the bone.
et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large;	 and such treatments are when the swelling is between the skin and the bone, and abscesses are small, so you should make a wide incision into the head.
et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre;	 And let it last as long as the moisture flows.
et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	 and this is the form of a swelling.
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If there is too much moisture and the abscess is larger, make two incisions shaped like a cross according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut:	 And if the moisture is under the bone, and you see signs of gaps in both ends of each part, and it feels sharply when pressed with your hand into the density, and this has not been set right.
si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	 if it is necessary to split between the head in three cuts according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	 After the incision, remove all the pus thoroughly.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor;	 After straightening the edges of cloth and powders, and putting wine and oil, leave it so until the fifth day.
puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	 Then remove it, and treat the wound with bandages and ointments, allowing the head to straighten evenly, and give the patient dry meat with a little moisture until the limb is comforted and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue;	 And another way of incision is to look at the size of the abscess and the gathering of water.
car aucune fois est elle devant;	 for it never lies before;
aucune fois derrier;	 for it never lies behind;
aucune fois en destre;	 for it never lies on the right;
et aucune fois en senestre.	 And never to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir;	 So that you may cut where there is an abscess, and the filling of water, and do according to your ability.
et warde que tu ne coper l’artere;	 And be careful not to cover the artery.
et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	 and have a flow of blood, so that the patient may die from its slowing and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	To restore
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When a disease called "catarrh" occurs in the eyes or groin and the illness is long-standing, and medicinal treatment does not help, then the last resort is to perform cauterization with the tool used to tie off the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief;	 It is therefore necessary, when you see it covered, that the patient raise his head again.
aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel;	 After rubbing the area with a rough cloth until the veins appear, then draw out all of the patient's collar.
puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues;	 Then look and see where the vein runs, and the lips of one and other are behind the ears, and few have returned.
puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	 First mark the edges of the wound with a tie, then cover both sides with a strip measuring two fingers in width, continuing until it reaches the bone or is as wide across the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see it, tie off the artery with a stitch from above and cut it just as two points cross over.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	When the vein is opened, blood flows continuously from it.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os;	 And if the vein does not open upon feeling it, you must measure a space of three fingers in length, then tie and cut up to the bone.
et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere;	 and ensure that the correct amount of blood is removed if it's six ounces or so, depending on what the patient can tolerate, and the filling of the artery.
puis regarde la plaie:	 then examine the wound:
s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 if it remains above the bone without a flap of skin, and there are no signs of an abscess when you cut into it, then strain the wound, bandage it, and apply poultice until it is healed.
de emigrainne	From gouty inflammation
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When gouty inflammation comes early and catarrh with moisture from tears and heat in temples and old headaches and such things occur, if it is treated by various medical methods of medicine and nothing benefits him, then we extract the arteries from the temples and cauterize them as we have discussed.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit;	 The manner of their extraction is such that the patient makes his hairs on the temples and listens to the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its pulsation, and is not easily replaced as with some men who are too cold.
et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement;	 And if it is replaced, the patient must strain their neck with a piece of cloth, then rub their head with an abrasive cloth, and apply warm water until the artery becomes clearly visible.
puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	 Then take the spatula whose form is as follows:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie;	 Then carefully scrape the skin until you reach the artery, then cut it at the edges with forceps, and separate well the threads that are opposite each part.
et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	 If the arrow is fine, then bind to the elbow's tip, and bandage that area according to the quantity of two joints.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	 If not properly reduced, it will never regain full function again at all.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III;	 And treat for six days up to three;
et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc;	 And if the arrow is large, it should be tied in two layers of strong, double-threaded silk cord to prevent rotting at the wound site and ensure blood flow.
puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez;	 Then bandage the excess between the two layers at the same time, and then, if you see fit, use the fire caustic cautery up to the bone until the joints are sealed.
et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	 This is the work done if the patient does not have a fever and is of warm constitution.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors:	 Because the fire cautery is used to end swellings.
por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	 For this reason, it is of greater assistance for swellings.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites;	 Or, when extracting the veins, one should fill the place with fine cotton and apply well-made bandages.
et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And when they are removed, use dry medicinal mixtures that promote healing and bandages until it is safe.
et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez;	 And if the artery is severely torn as you work on it, quickly apply heat with cautery, and place the location of vinegar there and stretch your hand so that the wound heals.
et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient;	 And if it is not apparent, then cover the place with mustard until the wound hardens, and apply cold water to the area until it ceases, and bind it as necessary.
et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	 And those who are skilled and more adept in the extraction of an artery should cauterize the vein with this sharp fire caustic at two parts, but the sharpness be well spaced to preserve heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when inflammation is too hot, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus;	 And it should have between the two knives a space of size I, and then when you grasp both edges with your hands, heat the iron until it glows up to the bone, and cut the vein in two parts.
et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout;	 and be distanced between the two eyes because this fire caustic is not suitable for all cases;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 and this is the form of the fire caustic:
des larmes	By tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	 When the tears from the eyes descend into veins near the forehead, and there is no benefit from medicines applied, and you see the patient's face turning red, and feel a pulsation in their temples as if with fear.
et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	 And those wounds are held and kept moist so that the hairs of the paper become detached, and the papers wither, and scorched by the heat of tears, if such care is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	 And they call it the "old contusion treatment," and you must do this to the patient who has this disease: shave the hair from his forehead, then make three cuts or equally spaced according to the width of the forehead.
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	 and one of the cuts shall be made so that it runs up the middle of the forehead to the hairline, and the others are placed two fingers above the eyebrows, but take care not to incise the arteries that lie two fingers above the eyebrows.
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	 And position your hand with the continuation of two jawbones, so each wound is as wide as three fingers' breadth.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	 And have an esponge and two cloth pieces to apply pressure for stopping the bleeding, then insert the styptic made of three parts as follows:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	 From the incision which goes from the temple up to the second incision.
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	 And scrape off all the core that is between the two openings completely through to the sac above the bone, then make a new cut from the middle incision up to the other second one, and then extract this styptic substance.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you put the instrument called "culterale" in the first cut, and it is very sharp on one side, but also soft so not cutting, and that is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	 And make the bandage cutting toward the chest near the heart, and the ribs soft to the bone, and continue until it reaches the middle crack.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	 And tie off all vessels coming from the head that are visible until the incision is continuous up to where the core opens, and then make another cut in the middle opening to the other end.
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	 And then extract blood evenly, and express the place to locate the taken blood.
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	 Then place a piece of fine cotton in each cut, and cover with cloths soaked in wine, oil, and honey, ensuring that abscesses do not form.
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And after three days heal the wounds, then apply a large amount of boiled water soak, followed by curing with basic oil of Basil, and other remedies used for treating wounds until they are well-healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the eye sockets
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	 When someone comes with severe and chronic inflammation, and you see the eyes swoln and small, causing blurred vision, and burnt papers.
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	 And the hair falls out, and at the top there is sharp pain, and the patient sneezes.
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	 Then from these incidents it is said that such matters and those chills come only from many veins, and the muezzin cares for where they are located, if so be this is true.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	 And you command the sick person to turn their head backward, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead, and another one twice as wide.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	 And it begins from the cut of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision reach the bone;
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	 and remove your hand from the glands in the temples that move during eating;
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	 and when the bone is revealed, let all the blood be absorbed by a sponge, then place it between the two lips of the incision and insert old cotton, and try with thread;
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	 Then lay the cloth soaked in wine and oil on top, and protect it from heat abscesses.
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	 When it is inflamed, if necessary, rub the bone until pus starts to form, then treat with things that dry out sores, encouraging healing of wounds.
En teil maniere:	 In such a way:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	 Take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of opium, and make into paste.
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	 Apply to these wounds to encourage healing completely.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Pour que tu puisse ceuele que les poilz le oinseu quil estropent lou poignons si sachant que li oui parsont; et si a qui peint, et si bien estroier de. Et si tu ne seroit pas plus bon.
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	 All that oozes from the ears is one of four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	 either grains of sand, or beast matter, or bits of stone, or similar substances like iron.
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	 or seed, such as crop residues, peas, and beans.
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	 Or when something flows out like water, easily and with similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	 When it bleeds in the ear stone or another manner of thing that does not adhere to the ear, nor grows within the ear, then set the ear on the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	 If you see the stone, if it drips any bit of violet oil or linseed oil, then perform an extraction.
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	 and the person has a condition causing them to sneeze, and they block their nostrils when sneezing occurs, and place cloth or woolen strips near the ears.
et estent l’oreille au desus.	 and stretch the ear upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	 It often happens by this treatment.
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	 and if it does not come forth, then a delicate extraction is performed with the following method:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	 If it comes out through the pinchers, that's good.
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	 if not, then perform an extraction with a fine filament of thin doubled thread;
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	 And if it does not come through there, make a funnel of iron and push the top of the funnel or small hole in the ear firmly, then stuff the area around the funnel with soft wax so that winds cannot enter.
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	 Then treat it with a form of fire, as often times wind comes in this way as we have mentioned;
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	 And if it does not come in any way, take pine resin and place the birds there, and use some instrument of sharp point for this purpose, and put some cotton around.
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	 Then press the pine resin onto the stone or any other thing, and treat with fire.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	 And if it does not come from any of the things we have said, hurry to split the ear so that pus may enter and there is a swelling.
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	 The manner of the incision is such that you first elevate the patient's head, and draw out the blood according to the measure of its virtue, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, making a small cut at the root of the ear near the fat or bone.
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	 And make the incision like a crescent, as you reach towards the bone, then squeeebreze it with your mouth powerfully.
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And apply the dressing until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	 And if there are pus and it swells, perform an incision for drainage.
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	 And if it cannot be drained, then prepare a spatulum gently in this manner:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	 And perform an incision on that stone.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	 But do not attempt this when you think the grain is soft due to ear moisture, until you have done it many times.
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	 Then carefully extract using tweezers and a sucking instrument, as we have said, so that the extraction is smooth.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	 Once the grain has thus entered into the ear, it is necessary for the patient to sneeze with a first conditioning, and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	 And be careful on that same ear where he is afflicted.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	 If it falls out by itself, this is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	 If not, if you take many pieces according to the length of your thread that are thin and light, heat them a bit in fire.
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	 And then instruct the patient to insert one or two pincers into his ear, and remove them from there with their pieces on the other side, and extract another stone underneath the stone that is in the ear.
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	 And continue to remove stones from stone to stone until all moisture has dried up and so it will heal completely.
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	 And if you see it, then take the joint and insert one head into the ear, and the other head remains until the less painful joint is achieved.
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	 Then reset the rest of the joints as needed until all are aligned, as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	 In extracting a thorn, if it is of small size, as though insignificant and similar to others, treat it as we have said in the section on surgery.
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	 but if it is a large thorn that can be felt, then prepare for using forceps for its removal.
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	 and this is the easier thing to remove which is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	 In extracting worms from the ears, as you care for them as we have said in the section on surgery and dealing with pus, if the treatment does not work, it is necessary to examine the ear under sunlight.
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	 If there are any worms, if they treat with subtle pinchers, and if they do not appear, then take the bone of which this form is.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	 And it must be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	 And insert the more subtle part into the ear according to the amount of the patient's suffering, then shape it fully with the bone.
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	 Do this often until all veins are healed.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	 And if they do not obey to be removed, then plug around the bone with cotton as I have said in the stone.
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	 and if they do not come out as we have said, then administer the dilutions that the ancients have tried in the incision of worms, and you will find or treat with dilutions.
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	 And if you drip your oils and medicines into the ear of this instrument, which is why it takes on such form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	 And [it] be made of silver or gilded brass from the small holes, and above them for pouring.
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	 And to ensure the pressure of distillation within an adequately made copper instrument for this purpose, and if you see [it], wrap it with tinder and cover around the tip promptly with cotton.
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	 Then pour your oil or juice, and what you see of your medicines into the vessel, and let it be in the ear.
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	 Then [you] fill up all the tinder with cotton and press your hand quickly as long as the oil is dripping or filling of the ear.
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	 And he feels pain inside, and there should be a distillation of the pus, which is then applied to fire as such that it's distilled in the ear.
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	 And ensure it is not too cold, for the medicines would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Pour que tu puisse ceuele que les poilz le oinseu quil estropent lou poignons si sachant que li oui parsont; et si a qui peint, et si bien estroier de. Et si tu ne seroit pas plus bon.
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	 No child is born without any eyebrows or ears.
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	 And this same thing happens at home due to bleeding from a wound or discharge in the ear, and these eflusions often come partly into the ear so that it cannot be seen.
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	 And sometimes there is no trace of bleeding, and he sees well again.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	 Therefore, if it comes into the ear and cannot be seen, it signifies a serious healing in various conditions, and when one sees this, you should place the patient's ear to the sun.
et regarde dedens:	 And look inside:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	 If you see swelling visible, then assess whether the operation involves all of this stretching area from which it takes shape:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	 And so be the ears and incision in front and behind, all flat, if they do not pierce the ear.
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	 If the swelling is from a jaw or body of the ear, take it with delicate tweezers and gently cleanse, until all bones are removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	 And if the swelling is found in the ear, take a fine and delicate razor and dry it slightly over fire, then return the body of the ear to its place.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	 If you sense swelling causing the patient pain upon hearing, pierce it lightly, and ensure not to burden the ear's nerves.
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	 Then insert a tent in the ear according to its width at the opening and grease with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	 Do this for any day until the wound is dry; then take a tent and apply fresh red mud, and powder with crushed vitriol.
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	 And if you see the ear flare up, it is fitting to strip off the tent and apply another tent with mud from a ceramic bowl mixed with rose oil and wax until the inflammation subsides.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then let it heal until it becomes healthy again.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if there is bleeding, soak a sponge and wrap in cold water, place it on the ear, and apply other treatments that remove blood discharge such as distillation therapy.
de la char des papieres	From the collection of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	 This ointment that comes from paper when it is wet and dry, you must extend with tongs and tweezers, and wrap the stem in a piece of spatulary root;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	 Then apply freshly crushed vitriol on top.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	 And if not removed by dissection, then cauterize with the pointed cautery after incision so it may move.
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	 and often repaired, as nothing remains from their roots;
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	 and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots become burnt and do not return.
de la gresle	les que he as a l'ard; that t s;t; puis quivide le ; theta; J.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	 Many times they come as paper-thin things that appear gritty in form and hardness, and thus this disease is called "granulation," consisting of a large amount of moisture above and below the skin.
li ovraiges est telz:	 its nature is such:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	 take heed if granulation moves on either side, and this is an easy thing to know;
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	 Make it wide open, then the scraping of each part gently, then take it with forceps, and bind it up.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	 If you cannot cover it without slightly piercing the paper, nothing will harm the patient.
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	 And if the crack is large, assemble with stitches and treat until it heals completely.
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	 And if it is small, do not apply too much pressure, as the ointments will restore it quickly and cause redness.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	 And if the bubo descends into the depth of the ear towards the upper area, reverse the paper and extend it with forceps, bandage, and press on both sides.
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	 And if the paper is moved by the incision, it causes no harm.
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	 When hail is collected, cleanse the oil of salted water, and treat the wound from which it originated until the patient recovers well.
de la graisse des eulz	And wash the wound thoroughly with water and soap to prevent infection.
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	 Epilepsy is a fat that arises in the loins from papers over, and it happens more often in children than adults, grievously affecting their eyes, causing them to have convulsions at dawn, and they cannot look at sunlight because tears rush to their eyes.
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	 And because of this, they lie on their faces downwards, sleep on their backs, and have swollen papers under their damp eyelids that appear covered by epilepse which manifests in the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	 And when you apply pressure to the joint with your hands, feeling something pass through inside.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	 And the manner of treatment is such that the patient places his head on a pillow.
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	 And then he takes a cloth of linen and makes a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity contained by each part, then places it on him.
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	 and press his thighs from both sides so that the swelling is gathered within the circle;
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	 then make an incision in the middle of the swelling with a sharp scalpel, and it should not be wider than the wound made on the vein's edge;
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	 and cut through the skin as you find the swelling.
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	 and in various cases, swelling arises from the incision, according to the shape of a white lump of fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	 Pull out all at once a piece of patched cloth between your two fingers towards the dislocation, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is scattered.
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	 And ensure that you do not pinch at the tear, that you do not spread it all over the area up to the bone, and do not crush it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	 And if the swelling does not open at the beginning of the tear, slightly elevate the tear until it opens.
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	 Then extract as we have said, then moisten cloths with warm water and vinegar, place them on the site, and bind it securely.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	 And for those men who grind and place them there to spoil the moisture that has lingered.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then the healer treats it until it is sound again.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if an abscess comes to a head, then the healer treats with warm plasters until it is sound again.
des poilz des papieres	of hair from paper strips
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	 When hairs appear that are misaligned and aged, they harm the eyes, and bring about familiar ailments like tearing and softening of the papers and algae, until it causes the destruction of the eyes.
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	 And there are four methods of treatment:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	 Or by fire caustery alone, or by medicinal ague according to what is prescribed in the chapter on caustery, and it is done either by incision and suturing or with poultices as I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	 It is necessary that you place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the page of oil to your left hand.
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	 if it turns well, it is good.
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	 if not, place an arrow through all the thread above.
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	 and be it near the edge of the paper or where hairs grow near these threads, cut the thread along all the paper, then turn it smoothly.
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	 Then make at the part below the parchment, below the hairs close to it, along the entire length of skin and tissue, from the great shoulder down to the small.
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	 Then extract the thread and place a small tent of cotton and cloth beneath the parchment, then sign on the parchament with an impression as like a raspberry leaf, ensuring that the figure is according to the quantity you see raised in the parchment which is exposed to all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	 And if there's a part that requires coping with a large quantity of the parchment according to how much the parchment is softened.
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	 Then make on all the tissue above the two lines that you have signed, and begin from the large shoulder down to small.
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	 And it should be one of the openings near natural hair growth in the skin's thickness at a root, then insert the needle into one of its corners with care, and scrape thoroughly.
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	 Then stitch together the two lips with a running stitch using one thread of fine woolen yarn, and drain any blood, and trim excess threads near both eyebrows without leaving anything sticky.
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	 And if not, do nothing about it, then leave the stitch and threads for three or four days.
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	 Then treat the wound without dry or constricting stitches as the paper becomes loose from the wound and its healing process, but the stitch is loosened (as the ancients say), which is a work without fear.
et si a une autre maniere:	 If by another method:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	 And you guide the paper into a shape similar to the hollow of a fir tree as we have described, with three times around in accordance with the form shown here.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cover what supports the small forces evenly according to the shape shown here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	 And if you cannot hold the tongs and the item is not evenly shaped, then take a needle or one with a single thread, and place it within the hollow of the fir tree.
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	 and take another thread near the larger branch, and the second thread near the smaller one, and join between them the threads evenly.
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin over which you have marked, as we have described, then unite the two edges of the wound by stitching them together, and heal until it is healthy.
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	 And if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar soothing oil.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	 And there are times when the hair of the papyrus is turned:
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	 If it becomes necessary to use what we have said about the incision.
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	 But the stitching on one side and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	 The treatment of ulcers follows this form:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	 And you shall convert the papyrus and extend it inside as I have said, then make the ulcers by craft, with fine threads as long as the width of the stretcher is wide.
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	 And cut at both ends where you hold the threads:

dou derrompement de toile uvee	The fall of a sheet or cloth used (in context likely referring to surgical dressing)
