de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of the nail's abscess
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	 A panaritium is an abscess that arises from under the nail of the thumb or toe, or sometimes appears in other fingers.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	 When it is neglected and not cared for, if an abscess comes, it will burn, boil, and flow with pus until the root of the nail is reached, and by chance may consume it entirely.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 And comes to the decay reaching the bone, causing a stench and pain, with shoulders wide apart, and discoloration is evident.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 When you treat it as we have explained in the section, and if the treatment does not succeed, then you must cut out all the excess tissue associated with the nail, and afterwards cauterize the wound.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	 Cauterization provides great aid if the bone is healthy, and the nail is sound.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	 And if the nail is consumed by worms and begins to point, and decay occurs, then you should cut off the root of the nail where the worm burrows, pour it upwards, and gently but thoroughly scrape away the substance, then apply medicines with burning and corrosive properties on the remaining area;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then treat with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	 And if there is decay in the bone, when cured and treated with force, because as long as the bone decays it is, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 and if you see the joint decaying, treat with force as previously mentioned, then treat until it is healed.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	 and if it is painful and swollen, and causing great pain, first you must anesthetize it.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	 then cut the thick nail with a transverse incision below it, but be careful that the cutting does not reach the quick which is under the nail, as the patient would feel too much pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 and if it occurs, put something on it to soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of dislocation is felt from below at the hand.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 The dislocation that is found in the hands of some men by chance is all flesh, and sometimes there are bones present, and at times none; these do not originate from the root of the joint where they are formed.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	 Those who are born with any deformity of the foreskin do not move, and those born at the junction of the foreskin may occasionally move.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	 The size of one who is plump should be lightened in this manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 Trim it at the root with a wide pair of scissors.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	 Those born in the junction's root are greatly difficult to cure:
si te tien dou coper.	 If you do it with care:
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For the one that originates from behind or beside the nearest bone, it is necessary to first cut around the flesh up to the bone, then cut the bone with an appropriate sawing motion, and then heal it until it is sound again.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	Dislocations arise from a joint being out of its place, occurring either by birth, or by incision wounds, or scorching with fire, or similar causes.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	 If it is necessary that you cut the swelling, so that it may heal according to its natural shapes:
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	 Then place between two tents or linen cloths wetted with oil of roses, so that they do not stick:
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	 Or you put between two pieces of fine gauze, until the lump is healed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If sensation comes to any of its fingers with the palm, then bandage accordingly as it should be.
des vils	 The wretched ones
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	 These are large wounds covered with excessive melancholic fluid, which come upon various body parts.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 And they more often occur in the legs of those who walk and work and carry things, than elsewhere.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must provide them relief from pus at any time, and then clean the bladder ache with camphor.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	 The treatment with iron is done in two ways:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	 the first is to wrap it and bleed black blood.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 The other method is to lift the vein, and tear it completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	 Healing follows this manner:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	 The first step is to bathe the leg in hot water until it becomes thoroughly softened, then hold the limb by the thigh up to the area below the hip and towards the outer part of the knee.
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	 Then make an incision in the area selected, either one, two, or three times wide. Next, extract and remove the black blood with your hand from one end to the other until the healing power of the sickly body is no longer able to bear it.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	 And then bind it up, instructing that they be nourished with meat-based black dye;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 And begin the evacuation and cleansing when the veins are filled, causing discomfort to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	 The movements of his limb are according to this manner:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	 Raise the patient's leg, if it has many hairs, then give him a bath, and rub his leg with hot water until it turns red, causing the veins to swell.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	 And if you do not have bathwater, heat it by fire and then apply the cloth to the veins long at the leg's top near the knee or below the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	 Then wrap it with cloth and scrape the veins from each side until they feel as if you can sense them.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	 And it is seen red and black, and when it enters or through leather appears like a whitish cord.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	 Then pull the thread out slowly as it passes through the skin, and then secure it to a light hook, then tie in another place on either side of the thighs.
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	 Then scrape the skin on either side of the vein until it appears, then lift up to the root as you have done, and tie it off with another ligature as before.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	 Then make a second tie or more if needed, then lift it up and secure to the hips, then pull tight until reaching the next tie.
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	 Then extract from knot to knot, ensuring all force is removed, then cut it off.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	 If you are unable to pull it and lift it up, then insert a strong, thick needle through the entire thread, piercing and pulling out both ends. Insert from under the skin, and turn your hand back and forth until it comes loose.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	 And ensure that it does not scar over, for if it scars over, it cannot be pulled or lifted out, and this causes harm to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	 And when you have fully extracted it, then place a cloth soaked in wine and oil over the wound site.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	 And if the vein is twisted and tangled together and not straight as we have said, then it should be cut lengthwise but do not cover it.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And the treatment as we have previously mentioned.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	 The form of iron used to make the cautery is curved, and does not cut, but holds the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 and it has a large curve because if it were subtle, it would cut the vein, but be thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
de la voinne civile	 of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	 This vein lies within legs, in hot areas where no grass or trees grow, and on land without moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 and sometimes it appears elsewhere than in legs, which occurs from swelling coming from under the skin, as it comes within the body with worms and veins, nestled between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 When the signs of this vein's beginning are such that it causes great swelling in the leg, then the lice change, and the vein begins to protrude outward, like a plant root.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	 When the shoulder is opened, it must be wrapped around with a piece of linen from one to two and a half cubits up to three cubits, leaving the wool on the leg, and every time there is no defect, wrap around with the linen, and the thread.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	 And if it is too long, then cut off a part of it and wrap the remainder around, but do not cover it completely at its root until it is entirely removed.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	 Because if you cut it, then pus enters the joint and brings about abscesses or rot there, causing a serious illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	 For this reason, it must be treated gradually until completely healed, leaving no remnants or debris behind.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	 And this vein should never be treated with hands for too long or abruptly. Once a man came to me whose vein was X palms in length. When it is cut, I amble the pus out and pierce it all the way through so that everything comes out.
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 And let it be emptied of any matter inside, and remedy at the site with mordant herbs for a certain period each day, then treat as one would an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	 And never wash the wound with hands or any other objects, especially when it is open at the joint of the arm, and there is much drainage, which causes swelling.
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 Treat it as we have previously mentioned.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 Between skin and flesh where new vessels arise
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	 This illness is known in our land as "the ox disease" because it frequently occurs in the veins and is caused by a small worm that lives between skin and flesh, traveling throughout the body rising and falling, causing significant discomfort from limb to limebefore it damages the skin or wherever it goes.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	 And it is caused by putrefaction of various bodily fluids, such as worms and snails and ascarids in the belly.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	 And there is doubt about its severity, because when it spreads through the body, and rises to the head, and comes to the eye, by chance entering, it destrobes the eye.
et ceu avient maintes fois.	 And this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	 When you see it being bled and milked, it cannot be stopped when it spreads:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	 So it is necessary that you tie the head above and below a strong joint tightly, then cut around it with a knife, and if the vein appears fully in the bile, and you cannot find it, then cauterize it with fire until it stops bleeding.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	 The greatest harm it causes is that blood vessels may rupture, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	 And if you see it approaching or close to the blood vessels, hold firmly onto its eyebrows, then clip and bind them.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 It is necessary for the patient to use bodily purification with solutions of medical substances against harmful humors and meat that has spoiled.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 From the pain which arises from swelling caused by wind.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	 This disease is called "wakir" in our land, and it brings pain to certain limbs, then moves from one member to another.
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 And I tell you as such.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	 I was called to a sick woman, and discovered her with swollen arms, and saw a small inflammation in the arm veins.
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	 And immediately afterward, the vein rises just like a worm in the shoulder, swifter than any other thing, as if silver when cut from one place to another.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	 And the pain departs from that spot, and shifts to the shoulder, and then shortly afterward runs through the entire body until it reaches the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 Then he told me how it returned within the body, as I have seen it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	by:
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	 Nevertheless, I wanted to maintain that the pain moved from one place to another, but I had not seen it in the woman as such.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	 and I thought that was because the woman had a dry body, her veins exposed, and hence appeared to have constant flatulence.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 And those who are dislocated due to this reason do not appear immediately as those with dry bodies and veins; and whose wounds have been healed.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	 And when you see treating this illness, and the patient feels that pain as we have said, then press above and below swiftly, and hold it until the swelling subsides to its place.
et cauterize le leu;	 and cauterize at the site.
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	 and if it is not visible to your eyes, then the treatment of those who swell up like foul pills, and sycamore seeds, and other similar things.
des saiettes	 Of arrow extractions
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	the pain: oughts (a, then heal sofes d, and if they ct; t;
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	 The variety of their cases is that there are those with large points, and small ones, and hairy, and smooth;
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	 And of those with two angles, and of those with tongues, and of those where it has protrusions.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	 and that which exits through any limb in either manner:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 or as principal members exiting (e.g., brain, heart, liver, stomach, kidnecks, intestines, bladder, and similar limbs).
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	 When it exits through any of these members, then the signs of death that I will tell you hereafter appear:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	 if one must consider extracting this arrowhead because death approaches in various ways.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 and when these bad signs do not appear, and the arrowhead is not fully embedded, then treat it as such, and heal the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	 When the arrowhead enters and pierces the bone, causing a sagging jaw above the brain, it results in blindness, pain, straining, reddening of eyes, inflammation and red tongue, mental disturbance with speech mixing, and bilious vomiting.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	 And sometimes there is loss of strength in the nose or ears.
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	 And occasionally it affects speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	 There is a discharge from the wound that appears like white hair, and oozes as red as fresh blood.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	 If these signs are evident, then proceed with the treatment, and extract the arrowhead if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	 The signs when the arrowhead penetrates or enters are as if it is near the left breast and feels like it has been driven into something hard, not hollow.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	 And sometimes the patient moves as well as hairs, with black blood in their veins, and they come coldness and cold sweat, and syncope.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	 Then there is doubt that death will follow.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	the durt; and there (as aul se ues benc!
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	 And if the arrow falls into the lower covering, it is near the small ribs;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	 and causes severe pain and sorrowful groaning.
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	 and they move all of the limb at the shoulder joints.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow enters into the belly, perhaps from a wound not affecting any of the indigestible meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow enters into the belly, and it does not pass through the intestines, there is no hope for a cure or extraction of the arrowhead.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	 And if the arrow falls into the bladder, causing it to leak and frequent urination, the patient feels strong pain.
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	 Know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other parts - as made by the collarbone, throat, shoulder, upper arm, spine of the back, forearm and legs, and similar limbs - are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it is not poisonous, as I shall tell you what happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	 It happened to a man whose arrow came out or close to the base of the neck root:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	 I tried it, and on the other side broke through the fat of the ear, and was sound without any harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	 And broke through one of the arrows that fell in the fat of the ear behind the paper, and the arrow was reinserted, unable to reach more than just the tip towards its base, and the arrowhead was large like a Turkish bow, easily without ears.
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	 The joint remained sound, and no harm befell it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	 And broke through an arrow in the throat to a Christian, and the arrowhead was Arabian with ears.
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	 I approached the Barbarians, and subtly as I tried to break through, the Christian remained unharmed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	 And treated an arrow wound at the belly, thinking it was fatal.
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	 and then after passing thirty days, his condition did not change.
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	 I cut around the arrow, skillfully maneuvered it, and successfully treated the wound without any complications.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	 And if you encounter a person with an arrow in their back where the wound is freshly made;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	 and if it remains inside them, without affecting their natural disposition or causing harm in any of their natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	 And you see another man where an arrow has struck his face and the wound is made fresh;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	 and it remained there causing them great pain.
et mout d’autres semblans.	 and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	 And injure an arrow at one of the king's men, which was lodged in his groin and slightly leaned to the right side.
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	 and the arrow was fully protruding.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	 I went called for treatment after it had been there for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	 If I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	 He holds all with subtle enticement, and she does not perceive it.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	 And he felt no pressure or pain from his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	 I thought it was due to the arrowhead's point. I placed upon him a poultice soothing and digestive, because his eyes were not inflamed;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 and it appeared that the wound from the arrowhead remained.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	 I applied the poultice for two days, and reopened the main wound, so that the patient suffered long times until he felt the arrow within his brain.
et il le me dist.	 and he told me this.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	 I applied medicinal acidic remedies to the wound for three days until it healed, and tried them, feeling the arrowhead head detach from its place.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	 Then instruct with the opening of the wound by that medical application, until the head of the arrow appears clearly.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	 And through it penetrated deeply within four months, and then I tried to push the wound as if using pincers, on one side and the other, but could not.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	 Then I ceased to subtly and ingeniously devise methods of extracting it, until I was able to grasp it in one day with well-made pincers, as the form will be presented at the end of this chapter, trying and keeping the wound open.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	 And the physicians judge that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	 I kept it open, and the wound was then stitched up, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	 Or I have told you the nature of extracting some arrows, so that you apply your care to what I do not mention here, for the book cannot possibly cover everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 But the wise masters compare few great things, and focus on what is currently happening and failing, working with nine works, nine instruments, at dealing with extraordinary occurrences in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	 I say that arrows are embedded in the members only where they have been driven by two methods:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	 or through the skin or elsewhere, or from another direction.
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 and that which pierces because of where it enters is an arrow penetrating into living tissue, and never does so at any other time.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	 And if it does not heal now, let it rest until the cartilage is fully regrown, and rejoined.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	 And also if it has been embedded in the bone, and cannot be removed, let it remain for some days, moving slightly each day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	 And then when it heals, and if it does not heal, carefully perforate throughout with a very fine needle, until the tissues are fully expanded, and then treat.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	 And if the arrowhead is embedded in the top of the skull and reaches close to one of the brain's cavities, along with any of the incidents I have openly mentioned to the patient.
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	 If it cannot be pulled out, but let it rest until even after some days, because if the arrowhead reaches near the spine, it is fatal.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	 If the arrowhead is lodged only in the bone and does not reach the sinew, and the patient suffers for some days without serious injury, then try to draw it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	 If it is stuck so tightly that it cannot be removed thus, apply cautery around it as I have told you.
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then treat the wound until it is cleaned thoroughly.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	 And if an arrowhead is replaced in the body and cannot be seen, then cover it completely with dressing.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	 And if you feel it, then use any suitable instrument.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	 And if you cannot for the widening of the wound or the deepening of the arrowhead and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, then bleed until the wound is large.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	 And remove the arrowhead if you can, and if it has ears that attach to where it's stuck in two parts you can see, break or bend these ears of the arrowhead as much as possible.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	 And skillfully, do not break the arrowhead, rather pull it out more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	:
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	 And if blood deterioration occurs in opposition, apply as we have said for treatment within this chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	 and be cautious with the incision of nerves and veins, apply method as you know how to extract the arrowhead without danger, whether soon or late, firmly or gently.
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	 and place the patient as they were when the arrowhead fell upon them, for it is the greatest aid that can be provided to them, and if you cannot do so directly, then follow what their signs indicate.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	 The arrowhead that comes from another direction, or through any parts of them, or if the skin is visibly swollen in the area:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	 Therefore cut down there, as long as the tongs can take hold, and then extract it.
si saut fuer maintenant.	 If swelling is now present.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, twist your round hand as much as it enters into the bone and widens the bone, then pull through.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	 And if it cannot come out, leave it for a while longer, and then resume the extraction as long as it can be taken out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	 and if there is an arrowhead present, strike at all of it;

et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	 and strike it again, so if you use an instrument with a pointed end to facilitate the extraction of the arrowhead.

et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And perform the healing until it is sound again.

puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	 Then grease the shoulder blade with a little bit of old oil; then place your left hand above that vein slightly below the bone where you wish to move it so that the vein does not burst upon striking.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	 For there are veins that flow like cords in the shoulder, and some are so full of swelling that when placed over the blade, it pulls back from the blade, cannot open the vein, and thus they become such.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	 And if it opens the vein, then the wound is too narrow, so one must be skilled in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	 And if the vein works on the first attempt, this is good.
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	 If not, start again slightly below where it was reset, unless the limb is swoln.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	 And if the limb is swollen, and the patient fears it, leave it for a day or two, and do not bind the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	 perhaps an abscess will come;
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	 nor give him a bath, then resume cleansing if he wishes to.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	 and if the boils are small, or he secretes blood subtly and you doubt that it is not as much blood as you see, probe that vein thoroughly.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	 and manipulate the wound slightly so that the limb becomes swollen.
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	 because this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	 If you see the joint swollen, do not begin to dissect again, and apply a little oil of roses, for it eases the body's pain and softens the tissue in this place with the oil.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	 And thus treat each vein you select with rose oil to stop the blood flow and seal it off.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	 Do likewise make tranching and binding when applied to the joint.
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	 If it is too large, carefully sever and separate it.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	 And if large abscesses occur frequently, especially when the vein opening is small and you act hastily, apply a damp sponge in water with some heat to it on the joint, and bind for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	 And it is necessary that you do this after the blood issue of the vein, and if it remains in place for several days without any blackness or greenish hue, then there is no harm.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	 And if you see anything of aloe or myrrh dissolved in a mixture with mint, it is a sign, ointment, or similar substance.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	 And often there occurs an abscess and appearance at the sanctity of the bladder:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	 So place your hand upon it, and if you find a soft lump under pressure with your hand, that is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	 Then avoid putting anything upon it as we have mentioned, for there may be no artery in the cord.
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 But make a dry plaster to harden the lump, then apply another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	 When blood is black, let it flow out until it becomes red.
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	 And if you see large veins, allow them to be drained until they are thinned.
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	 If it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	 And it is necessary for those who are flat and bald, and require blood extraction, to create a wider wound with broad edges.

et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	 This manner of maintenance prevents blood stasis and nerve compression, and is better to be done longitudinally rather than broadly.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	 And for those whose body requires maintenance, give them mashed apples in pear juice.
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	 If it is scalded, rinse with blood three or four times; and if it has a cold complexion, provide for the patient bread soaked in syrup sweetened with honey, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, with an agreeable scent.

If it occurs at the temple, after the issue of a great amount of blood, then one should inhale a mixture of charcoal and odorous syrup, and use other things that we have mentioned in the chapter on syncope for the evacuation of blood.

And if he wants to drain his arms, and use leeches at other times as needed, when they are greatly swollen by moisture, let him bleed a little bit and a little bit continuously depending on the quantity of his vitality.

si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	 If it requires expressing a large quantity of it and dilating the pores until they are full with sweat.

ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	 If it [the head of the shoulder] has gone out, extend the arm quickly, for that would be bad.

ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	 or you do not touch the dry sore, until the blood which has clotted in the vein flows again, and place slightly moistened dressing on it, and press lightly.

Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein under the arm is bled where the head of the vein lies because it is composed in that manner.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	 And the manner of healing is that the patient dips their hand in warm water until the dressing becomes red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	 then bind it moderately so that the veins appear well, and now heal across rather than wide or long.

et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	 And if it is like this, do not push the hand back into hot water again, because in winter it goes further than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	 And the vein of this hand is more saved from all other wounds, as there are no clots or nerves in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	 The vein of the thumb on the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is how it's done:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	 Strain the hand, and place it in hot water until the veins are filled with blood.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	 If the limb is twisted, and if you cut along its entire length, then do not injure anything.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	 And do not cut too deeply, for the nerves lie close together and intertwined; then return the hand to warm water if it is frozen in the wound and cannot be removed.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have addressed the bleeding as much as necessary, apply oil and wax to the vein and quickly join them together, doing this with each thread.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The remedy for the illness in the left hand is as follows, do exactly as I have told you with the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	 The physician of the knee is effective for all diseases under the body such as joint pains, retention of urine, diseases of the kidneys, and old ailments of hips and legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	 And the quality of its healing is that the patient must put their foot in warm water and rub it until it softens, and lay over the bone joint.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	 and the swelling is at the ankle, and from the foot go out many veins.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	 Then cut the bandage or make it wider around the ankle as needed.

et soit li flaimes anesil.	 And let there be a slight indentation.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the sinew cannot exit, reset the foot in water, and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	 If the physician fails at first, repeat again after some time, as the joint is stiffened.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	 Do not doubt of a nerve, as we have said, and thus make an incision on the other limb equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The head of the sciatic nerve is at the ankle near strong, and its irritation causes pain in the thigh when it's due to blood heat.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	 And the quality of his injury is such that the patient lies in a bath and extends above the ankle four fingers by twisting, otherwise he does not open the vein.
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	 and if it opens, then cleanse the wound in all ways that you can, and across.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	 and let them move as you scrape, for the joint is loose, and it is much more protruded than normal.
