des sainies de ventouse	 Of the buboes of cupping therapy
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	 Vents are made of horns, or animal hairs, or glass.
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	 And the evacuation is done according to two methods:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	 either by hitting and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	 And this evacuation that is done without a hit also follows two methods:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	 either by very hot heat, or without heat.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	 And evacuation done with a hit and blood extraction is performed in 14 parts of the body, some are entirely at the head.
et li autres est emmi le col;	 The other one is within the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	 and others are in two sides of the neck.
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	 and the pincers from below the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	 and the pincers at both shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	 and the pincers on the elbows;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	 and the pincers within both arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	 and the pincers in both legs.
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	 and the pincers on both ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	 and the bleeding does not involve any blood vessels, but rather small veins scattered in the flesh, so it is not painful to anyone, as with draining of veins.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 and it must not be inflamed or scorched with any fire or heat, in no illness that arises from congestion, until all the body has been emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	 And if it is necessary for illnesses or customs, we must examine each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and between every hour.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	 For there are those who, when they need to be examined, feel heavy pressure.
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	 and for those who experience congestion and redness on their face, in their head, and at the neck, along with darkening of the eyes.
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	 and those who experience blood spots in their mouth, swollen tongue, and bleeding.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	 and there are those who think, see through blood-filled and painful eyes and deathly things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we observe these signs, especially in the middle of the month, we order to bleed after 3 and a half hours past noon.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	 The medicine for the ears is helpful in easing the head's distress... it comes to the eyes, and one should not do this until all bodily fluids have been evacuated.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	 This ventilation is at the site of the head's cavity, and it should only be used by those with a cold complexion or who have weaknesses, as it causes them great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	 And therefore one should not use it without the guidance of a physician, nor by those with cold head diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	the unt les deux they are;
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	 Ventilation through the neck is at the site of the cavities in the head and abdomen, and thus it causes stretching of the bowels, cutting into the channel of the phlegm, and other issues, and distension.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	 It should not be done too forcefully, for if it holds too tightly, it can cause injury to the liver or heart and soul.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	 The ventriculation of II ribs by the collarbone causes pain in the head, otalmia and migraine, strangling, pain at the roots of the teeth, and is located near the sanctuary of the basilica.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	 And it is proper to command the surgeon that he express his hand in putting it on, not cutting the artery and avoiding any bleeding out of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	 The ventriculation below the chin causes mouth disease, gum decay, and various diseases found in the mouth.
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	 It is located near the sanctuary of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Incisions in the shoulders indicate diseases that arise from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	 The ventriculation of the elbows causes as much pain as from the three veins of the arm since it draws blood from these large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	 And instruct the surgeon not to pierce too deeply, for the flesh is tender and contains veins and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	 The catheter placed on the buttocks is useful for hemorrhoids and conditions below, and it should be large in diameter and made of wool, requiring proper pulling.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	 and sometimes, if she were too thin, she would break.
et i fai grans plaies.	 and this causes large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	 Legs' catheters drain well, for they draw blood from the entire body, and are effective against old pains of the kidneys, joints, and bladder, and promote healing.
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	 They are placed above the knees and ankles, and in all cases, they relieve the body after prolonged use, and bring about swelling in various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	 The way to apply the cupping is that you place it first empty, and do so quickly, and put it on hastily, and move equally, and continue doing so until you see it reddened and swoln, and with a dusky blood color.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	 Then remove, and reset the cups, and observe the condition of the body parts, for there are some with scars, and clear pores.
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	 If it is necessary to pierce once only, then make wide and somewhat deep incisions.
et suce legierement.	 and gently draw blood.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	 And if the vein is large, it should be punctured twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	 the first time to thin out the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	 And if the vein is very dense, it should be punctured a third time:
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	 And when we wish to draw blood little by little, it is just once with a lancet.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	 And if we wish to obtain much blood, we repeat the process often.
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	 And if the vein is narrow, use forceful pressure and ensure it ends such that the core is pierced quickly, and for those with thick and hard skin, as well as swollen parts, you should apply hot oil poultices to soften.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	 if it is so in that case, use purple oil or almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 and if it is inflamed, use chervil oil or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or other similar ones.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excesses are large and cold, take oil of myrrh, or balm-oil, or aniseed oil, and similar substances.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 If the one to whom you provide a tender and broad bandage does not need oil, then it should be washed after ventosation with rose water, or cold water, or blackthorn berry water, or gourd water, or porcelain stone water, or any similar liquid.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those with excessive moisture should rise easily, using myrtle water or sumac and other similar substances.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	 Those who have large excesses rise from old wine or water of aloe, or a concoction of anise or chamomile, or similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	 and they must not exercise breathing into the bladder before or during a bath, but after the bath one to two hours later.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 and they must not sleep after the ventosation, and it is necessary that they take a bath when needed for ventosation and when they have been vented.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	 And those who are sick with colic must warm themselves up if they feel too cold and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	 If it is necessary to grasp cold things such as ripe pomegranates and endive and lettuce easily, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 And mince pieces of meat, and broth from a cauldron, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	 And those with a cold constitution should grasp syrup of honey, and moderately aged wine that is neither old nor new, along with small morsels, minced pieces, and small birds and pigeons.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	 and on the day he resumes his activities, he should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	 it is appropriate to give certain individuals some triacle or musk before dislocation, or afterward, to strengthen the main limbs.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 and let them be sweetened without adding anything, but only for those who are hot, they should drink it plainly.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	 The suction cups that are placed without causing pain are those applied over the liver, and joints such as gouty toes, podagra, and over the abdomen, buttocks, legs, and armpits, because these body parts do not tolerate being pierced anywhere, and it is only done in order to draw blood from a limb back into another part, just as we do on the nipples when they are inflamed;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	 to remove the thickening present in the limb, just as we apply suction cups over the abdomen and buttocks to reduce the limb.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	 and alleviate pain when there is edema or stone, if you remove it by its attracting nature perhaps the edema, or restore the stone to its original position.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	 And thus it is done when placed upon the liver and kidneys with retained windwaters, and these bladders are prepared empty to draw out as much fluid.
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 And never are they arranged with fire, nor filled with cold water like maladies causing excessive sweating; thus the bladder is filled with hot water boiled or water that has had certain medicinal herbs steeped in it.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction cup administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	 And it should have two pieces of leather each half a palm wide at the base, and with holes around its circumference like for threading a needle, and be made from deer skin on the front so that it does not slip when placed upon the limb.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	 And it has among its tools a rod of crossbar made of brass or iron to put on a poultice, and they are large and small according to the diseases and condition of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 Because children's cupping therapy is different from that for adults, and it varies between thinness and heaviness.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	 And should this cupping be applied to the limb thus:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	 Take the poultice of wax or salve and place it amidst the cupping within the rod that lies across the cupping area, so that the heat does not burn the patient at the bottom of the cupping.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	 And then place it upon the limb, and you should do so at the percussion points we have mentioned before, such that when desired, steam will rise, and one may remove the cupping.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And apply a splint as before; begin again often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	 In the blister that is made for pneumonia treatment immediately, without an erect penis or scrotum, and it's only dressed when full of fluid, and placed over the limb fully.
et c’est li forme:	 and this is its shape:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	 Blisters are not dressed unless in limbs where you cannot place blisters due to smallness, such as lips and gums, for example.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	 and on naked areas of the body like ears or nose, and others similarly shaped.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	 and the quality of their use is that when you find blisters filled with soft clear liquid not causing trouble, take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	 And they place her on an elevated bed with a gentle pillow, until she is accustomed to it, and has no discomfort in the belly.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	 Then you shall wash with vinegar and a compress, then rub the limb until it is reddened, and apply bandages.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 And when they are filled and swollen, if it is possible to place a compress there, then apply one, as this works very well afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	 If not, raise the limb easily, and then pour vinegar on it abundantly, and then press out.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	 And if the wound still hurts after dressing the body with bandages, then apply a linen cloth soaked in cold water, and leave it on until the swelling subsides.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	 If there are multiple abscesses, apply crushed vitriol or gallnuts, and similar substances, until they have dried up.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	 Or place on the half-moon section of scraped veils, and let them dry until they harden in that area, thus sealing it now.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 And if further action is needed, then take additional materials.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	 And if the materials do not adhere, rub the blood-soaked area with fresh blood or insert a needle until the abscess opens, and then apply them, allowing them to dry as soon as they feel the blood.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 And when you see that they bleed, sprinkle some ground alum or crushed wool, or ash, and it will harden now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	the d.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These chapters are often necessary in the art of medicine, and involve the repair and replenishment of breaks and moisture loss.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	 Know well, dear student, that the madman seeks wisdom from this treatise, which he has never seen in any ancient book nor read.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	 And for this reason, such knowledge is strange to our land, for I have never found a good one (book).
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	 and I know nothing of it from the knowledge in ancient books, which I have studied so much that I am familiar with its teachings, through experiments, and by habit over my lifetime.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 And I have described in this treatise what is contained within it, and abbreviated at the end, clearly showing the forms of the distortions that are treated, as I have done in these two preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we must say that the preface of this book contains the essence of its words and chapters where the wise apply their understanding, dwelling on truth so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	 When any breakage or dislocation or torsions or strains occur in any part, it is necessary to support the patient on both sides with a splint, if nothing entirely supports them, as would befit their age, whether children, adolescents, or elders.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	 If the tension is not too great or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	 And avoid very cold things such as cold baths, and meats of birds or rabbits, do not drink wine nor consume any fatty foods, and do not fill up excessively with foods that cause the veins to be filled with blood until there is no doubt of a hot abscess, or spreading matter in the limb;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 If the patient returns to his first state of health, which he previously experienced.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that cause heavy nourishment, or viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and beef, lamb, pork, veal, eggs, fresh fish, strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For certain heavy nourishment represents moisture and more rapid healing of the fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	 And know that broken and old bones cannot be well repaired or joined according to their nature for the support of limbs, nor those also who are too tender, like the bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	 but pay no heed to joining the large tendons which are stiff and join the limb together, until it is strengthened as it was before.
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 and do not finish all his work, and for this reason he should nourish himself with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures occur in various ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	When the fracture of the head is different from that of the arm or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that resemble an arc and others by sharpening, like the tip of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture along a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	 And in every way have his appetite, and his own proper tools for restoration, according to what memory comes to him.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	 And it is known as a broken bone because the limb is twisted and quite open on one side, and lies close to the press of the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	 And when there is no twist or touch on it, and the patient does not feel much pain, unless there is a fracture.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 But it can well have a twist, a split, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not necessary to move your hand at all, but apply the following remedies immediately and then gently strain now subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	 And know that the fracture hanging down, and are two parts disjoined, now they must be made equal lest it become an abscess.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	 And if the abscess arises therein, let him not delay any day until the abscess is soothed.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	 Then make them equal to what you can easily and healthily move, and know that the restoration of it is easier than in those where there are fragments.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 Then restrain as appropriate thereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	 And if the bone is in pieces and it extends on two parts, whether it's arms or legs, or to your hand if it's small members, or two tendons, or one tendon and your hand.
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	 And place the member according to its natural form, so that if the parts of the broken limb are separated, you reset them by any means to their original positions as they can be moved, and ensure through your crafting no injury or pain comes to the patient.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 And properly align the two ends of the bone according to the best possible forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	 And feel well with your hand if it seems not rightly done:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	 If the reduction is done well, and do not strain it too much, nor press as those who induce abscesses hot and constriction in the limb have seen us many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	 And when the limb is at its limit, so gently restrain the patient that they do not move it, neither while awake nor sleeping, nor turning or in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 and ensure well that the limb is secured so that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	 For when it feels no pain, it is not at its limit and one must place it in such a way that it feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	 and you must ensure that it is positioned correctly, so that twisting does not occur when restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 And the condition of the broken limb is as follows, just as I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	; that he est la:  (e patience de se mar :
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	 For there are small members such as bones and tendons:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	 If it is necessary to wrap with thin and delicate linen cloths;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	 And those that are large, such as thighs and legs:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	 If it is necessary to wrap with a wide and strong ligature, because the wide ligatures encircle the entire large limb equally on all sides so that there are no irregularities.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	 Then it is tied with light padding for three or four turns depending on the limb, and the hand is slightly tightened along the entire ligature, then moved to above the fracture and loosened there, so that the breakage moves slightly away.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	 And soften the ties a little at a time, until you grasp a significant portion of the joint's natural state, then take up another tie, and return it correctly to its original position.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	 Then go back to the part without the breakage, and strain it moderately, neither too much nor too little, as we have said in the first instruction above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 Then place between the stitches linen or cloth so that they are all evenly matched, then secure everything above the binding, and then put in well-made stays underneath, unless there is an abscess or inflammation.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	 And if there is inflammation or an abscess, put on something soothing for the abscess heat, and that removes the inflammamo.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 Then strain the affected bones and have them bound with a wide leather strap or wood for splints, as shown in this diagram.
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	 But it is necessary that the affected bone placed on the break should be slightly larger and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	 and so also long as needed for small or large limbs;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	 then strained on the bones in the same manner as the first splint above the fracture, and tied with a thread if necessary.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	 more tightly it is, the less so;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	 and it should be moderate in thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of fine flax.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 because if the thread is thick as I have seen with works of folks who make their linen cord reels coiled up, it's a great mistake, for the splint cannot be evenly distributed if it is too fine, and it must not have less than two inches space between each bone.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is in pain from the heads of the pins after being tightened to healthy places, then place cotton or linen rags on them so they do not slip out.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the fracture, and the bone is broken, I will tell you the treatment as follows:
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to extract all shattered bones on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	 When the limb is large, it does not require immediate dressing but rather after 5 or 7 days, or more depending on the risk of infection.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	 And then follow the manner of ancient embalmings to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 And take some flour that is held against the mill walls, and mix it with abundance of egg, and apply this concoction, not too clear nor too thick, and use it, for it is a common way to restore fractures in various positions, especially in women and small children, as it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	 Another method of embalming that restores fractures, dislocations, and twists:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	 Take bile, aloes, onion, aspetide and frankincense, and myrrh, one spoonful each.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	 Mirrorwort and aloes, five spoonfuls each.
alechil VIIII З.;	 Alecites, nine spoonfuls;
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	 And make powder, and mix with honey and egg white;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	 If the patient's constitution is hot, use this plaster because it has good composition and quickly mends broken bones, benefiting many individuals.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	 Another kind of plaster that works for twisted injuries:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	 Take myrrh and violet leaves, one spoonful each.
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	 Mirrorwort and alechites, nine spoonfuls each.
acaice VI З.;	 Acacia, six spoonfuls;
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 On Wednesday of the Fast of St. Martin, boil Armenian spices with wine or plentiful water and conserve it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	 Another method to reset dislocated joints and bones from their place, which alleviates the pain that occurs, and it is used for breaking the bone and fractures.
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Take new linens, soak them in ease and cooked oil, and place it upon the wound.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 These bandages do not restore, but they are good for soothing a hot abscess and properly alleviating the pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	 Another method to reset broken bones that restore their integrity:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	 Take dried leaves of the fig tree and earthly parrot's leaves, grind them together, and use as a splint.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another way to bandage is for the healing of broken bones and remaining abscesses.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	 Take root of wormwood, chamomile, flowers of violets, and barley meal, one part from each;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 And you mix it, and with wine, and if the limb is swollen, then with vinegar mixed with wet coriander water or plain water, and apply it in use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another way of plastering more effectively than the first, when an abscess is ready to heal on its own in member restoration.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	 Take roots of valerian, and flaxseed, balm, honey locust, and sage, and flowers of violets and chamomile, all in equal parts.
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 And you grind them, and cook with salt water or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its resting state.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras states in his book that nothing else should be applied to the broken limb for healing other than a mixture made of wax and oil, and it should not be too hard or too soft within two layers.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen seems to suggest that dry and slightly warm substances should be applied to the broken limb for healing, such as myrrh, aloe, incense, and similar things, as we have mentioned.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	 Another method of balm that is suitable for injury and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	 Take the shavings and feathers of cocks or bird's quills, valerian root, and equal amounts of each; grind them up, and make an ointment from it and apply it thereon.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	 And then slightly move it again, and be careful if the patient feels no pain or has not moved the bone back to its place.
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	 If you do not manage to relocate by hand.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	 And if pain comes to the place, or itching, a sense of rest, or swelling occurs, hurry and relocate, and remove the splint now.
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	 and take light bandage, and use a damp sponge, and soak in water, and lift the place up until itching stops and pain is eased.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	 then let the limb rest for an hour, then apply dry cloth, moistened in water or rose oil, and wrap it up with a bandage until you are sure of heat from abscess.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	 And place it on the inflammation of the limb, and if there is bone pain, then resume gentle movement, and a little mustard plaster, and do not stretch it as tightly as before.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Resume subtle movements until they are suitable.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that abscesses and redness and pain and swelling are throughout the bone, and you need plaster and ligation, then begin again as before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	 And if nothing comes to the limb as we have said, do not reset it except after 3 or 4 or 5 or 7 days.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	 and never leave it for 20 days, as we see that until the fracture heals, approach the joint above.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	 then reset it more than first time, and let the wound swell with flesh, as I have said before.
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	 and if you see that it dries more than necessary, know that there will be no healing.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	 Rose from warm water every time you dislocate it, and do so daily, letting it rest a while.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	 So in this treatment also sever the nerves of the limb and quickly remove what are done by the ignorant physician who return the limb wrongly.
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 It is bad and such treatments are fearsome, and I see nothing else but the lazy ones and those who work directly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various ways of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	 There are many ways of fractures, and various shapes, and the causes differ;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	 for there are fractures caused by the impact of a sword, and the bones all shatter down to the fascia which is below the bone, as if struck with an axe or club;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 And because of this, this manner of fracture is called "hachure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	 Or the sword breaks the bone above without piercing, and this manner of fracture is called "absolute";
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	 And there are wounds from these two types of large or small fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it is impacted, cracked, or from striking against stone, falling on stones, or similar occurrences.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is an open fracture reaching the skin just below or above the bone, and this wound can be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	 And if there is a wound that heals in the bone as subtle as mouse hairs, and it is a small crack, and therefore this fracture is called "capillary";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	 And if the wound is made by being pierced with an arrow, or falling, or similar thing, and causes displacement of the bone piece upwards, and it fills in as smoothly as blacksmiths when they pour into molds.
si entre li piere dedens.	 If between the stones within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	 And this happens more often to those with bones that are mostly moist, as in children's cases;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	 and occurs in all these ways of fractures where small pieces become dislodged like marbles;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	 And I will speak about it on site.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	All know the methods of fractures through pulling apart, and examination with tests, and by the corrupt bone that lies beneath.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is known when the bone is discovered, and if it is rubbed hard underneath, an open black break occurs.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a break, beware in case of an accident with the patient; and if you see any malicious accidents such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, extension, paleness, fever ague, eyes protruding outwards and reddening, and other similar conditions, do not heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an unstable injury with hope for healing, begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the inflammation comes first to you, and it is winter, then on the fourteenth day you should remove the bone that you can reach.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is summer, then hasten to remove the bn before the seventh day so that the tissue around the bone becomes corrupted, and they come to the accidents we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	 And if the bone fracture reaches near the cloth covering the brain, then it is necessary that you split the affected part thusly;
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	 and that you grasp the injured head with care, exposing all sides of the bone as much as possible, and gently uncover the wound area more delicately than you can, and if blood flow occurs during exposure, or pus appears, assist it with what is appropriate, and ensure that you fill the cavity with soaked linen in oil-soaked rose petals;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	 And let the wound rest until the abscess is calmed, and ensure that blood flow resumes.
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	 Then begin working within the bone to remove it, and this is done according to two methods of treatment:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	 The first method involves cutting a narrow slit in front, and that is the shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another larger incision than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	 And the second method involves having various cuts of different widths, some narrow and others wide, with points, made of specially crafted iron:
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	 and working lightly so as not to fracture the skull.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	 And if the bone is thick and hard, it is necessary to pierce around it so that you make cuts with scrapers, not too deep into the skull or beyond the other test (presumably 'test' refers to a piece of equipment), which should have a margin or circle at the tip, so as not to go past the bone.
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	 And you must have several tools if anyone comes in the place of the spine's bone, so that you have tongs for all examinations.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	 and this is the form of three ways to use tongs:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	 The quality for examining within the broken bone is to place one pair of tongs on the bone and rotate with both hands until you know that the bone is fractured.
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	 then move the tongs to another place shortly after, and thus do it throughout, then use the scalpel to create space in the bone where it is broken, making the cut more delicately than possible, gently, as we have said, until you feel the bone with your hand or any of the instruments that you have like pincers.
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	 And ensure you do not touch the brain or the spleen.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	 And when you have pierced the bone and exposed it, and it is necessary to cut out the protrusion that has been left by the bone from any other instrument similar to a chisel, but it must be finer and more delicate than the other chisel.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	 And if there are no small bones or scales left, gently rub with any of the tools mentioned earlier.
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	 Then treat the wound as we have previously described.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	 And another method of treatment is that which Galen describes, and it is more effective.
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	 and the remedy must be strong, as he said.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you open part of the bone where the fracture opens up, and when you have discovered that part, place atop its head a lens-shaped incision tool so that it takes this form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	 And do not cut too deep, for it is an inflamed area on both sides, so that the one cutting towards the bone.
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	 Then gently strike with a small mallet above it, so that you lightly chip the bone all around, and take care not to hit the surrounding tissue.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 If it is exposed to the bone, gently chip away at the bone carefully, because doing so without harm and with caution is of concern.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the fracture of the bone does not penetrate all the way through to the skin, and the bone is cut mostly above it, leaving small pieces, then you must treat the inflammation, and have various subtle rasps from which you should extract scales in each place as deemed most appropriate according to the work and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If there are many coarse rasps followed by more subtle ones, continue doing so until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	 In each of these hair treatments and subtle fractures, it is necessary to align according to its direction.
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	 And this is something not properly restored by those who have studied in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	 And if the wound is severe, it's necessary to take a linen bandage according to the quantity of the wound, and soak in oil roseate (reddish oil), and place it on the w지디.
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	 Then take another cloth folded in two or three layers, and soak it with wine and oil mixed together, and place it over the first layer.
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	 And do this more gently than you can manage, so as not to burden the patient excessively, then administer it above the other layer without tightening too much until it only covers the wound.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	 And leave it like this for one day or two, until the abscess is calmed down, then remove it and apply medicines as herbs of lilyroot, flour of cumin, powdered incense, aristolochia, among other things.
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	 And make a paste from these things and apply to the wound, then administer healing medicines without burning.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	 Ensure the wound is clean and clear, do not leave any ointment or allow a boil to form, for when a boil forms on the cloth of the brain, it festers and pains the patient greatly.
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	 Because if you place something sharp on the skin, do not press down upon it.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, be cautious because if anything unfortunate occurs to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	 And if darkness does not come as a result of the medicine placed upon it, then you must mix one part honey and three parts rose oil in a cloth, and apply it to the affected area.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then proceed with various treatments as needed until healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	 Know that at no time are the two parts of the knee broken or separated, for they consist of only two bones.
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	 And those that are dislocated are cartilaginous, and do not break or snap, but rather hinge or twist, and then heal.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	 And if one of the two parts is broken, you must splint your index finger or little toe with bandages on both sides, and align the fracture within your index finger and ankle inwardly until they regain their natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	 And do this gently, ensuring that the patient does not feel pain from your treatment.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	If the fracture is in the part above the nose and it cannot be brought to its place, you should adjust it equal with a bit of a rod.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	 And if it is a fracture of both parts, do as described above, and hurry to restore its position the first day if possible.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	 If not, after the seventh or latest day, when the swelling has calmed down, then bind to the top of the injured toe with linden cloth bandages, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	 When you bind another on the other side, if there is a fracture there.
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	 And be that they are swollen to such an extent that they fill up the nostrils with snot.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	 And a healer said that you must anoint the tendons with butter, and change it each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	 It seems to me not well enough, but it should be made into a mixture of egg whites and flour, and mill powder.
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	 Then let the swelling stay as long as the bone is set, and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	 And never put goose nose droppings in place of the swelling, and if to it a sheaf of hay is placed around, and keeps the fracture, and blows on the patient's face.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	 Or do whatever you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to the neck while you are working on it, then place a compress or cotton cloth in rose oil, or with a little bit of diachronic (ointment).
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	 And if abscesses do not arise, then apply plaster promptly, of wheat flour and incense powder, mixed with egg whites, then place it on light cotton wool, but do not tie the nostr grooves.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	 If the break of the nose is small and it is broken into tiny pieces, extract as with suitable tools, then cut the fissure, and treat various difficult wounds and burns, and poultices and ointments appropriate for this.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If there is no internal injury to the nose, treat with bandages and apply linen soaked in broth until healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	For fractures of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is fractured but there is no open wound and the break is not too severe, as if it has been broken with a stick, you can see it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	 It is necessary, if the breakage is on the right side, that you insert your index finger into the patient's mouth.
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	 and if the breakage is on the left jawbone, insert your index finger of the right hand, gently push inward, then adjust with the other hand accordingly and ensure it's level.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is dislocated in two places, it is necessary to arrange for an expansion by two parts so that they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	 If there are movements of the teeth or bruxism, then they should be strained with a thread of gold or silver or silk, and apply cerate on the fractured jawbone, and place it under a double cloth.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	 And place the great splint well made under it, or an equal piece of leather long and wide according to the jawbone, securely fastening it in all movements that may occur, instructing the patient to rest, and suggesting they consume light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	 And if you see that the face changes, reset it every day, then restore what is changing back to its original state.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	 and place plaster over it, with finely ground powder or meal of chickpeas after removing the cerate.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	 And place a light linen on the dislocation, and if the dislocated bone touches, do not change the patient's position until it is properly aligned.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	 Often healed within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And when an abscess comes, arrange it as we have said many times before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	 And if there is a break and wound together, ensure no piece of bone remains exposed.
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	 If delicate in the vicinity where the swelling has settled near.

de la forcele	The strength of arms
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	 The shaft breaks many times at the shoulder, with breakage occurring in three different ways:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	 When it is broken and displaced into two parts, and there are fragments, making it easier to repair.
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	 Or when the break also includes an open wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	 And the procedures are as follows when the break with an open wound occurs: you must have two assistants, one of whom bandages the shoulder with the broken shaft.
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	 and the other should extend their arm towards the affected area.
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	 Then position the break evenly against your own shoulders so that it is as necessary, ensuring there are no visible misalignments or discomforts.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	 And if you require further extension, place a round rod made of cloth or linen under the patient's shoulder, with its thickness according to necessity.
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 Et ils sont étendus et livrés à leur force, et retenez-les dans votre main, de sorte que vous les positionniez correctement, comme cela se doit.

And if you cannot pull the head of the shoulder back due to it coming from the front, it is necessary for the patient to lie over their sling, and place under the shoulder .i. arm splint with a middle hole, and push in the ministers' hands downward until the shoulder bone is elevated.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	 And then bring the break close to your hands, and if you see fragments, it is necessary that you split above.
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	 and grip the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot join due to any protrusion, provide support with one of your cutting instruments.
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	 but use this instrument to hold them apart to protect against infection.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	 and make it resemble a spoon, not too deep, and as wide as needed according to the size of the bone and the strength of your hand.
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	 and it should have two ends, as you see, one end wide, the other narrow, according to the shape of the wound that you made when you treated the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	 And when you are sure of an abscess being hot, if the wound is large, or if you doubt a hot abscess, then cover the wound with linen and cloths, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess comes about, apply oil-soaked cloths, lint, and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	 The tension of a bone, when it is without wounds and not swollen, place plaster powder from the mill and whey butter on it, and put light bandages over that, and if necessary, use a splint underneath.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	 Then take a very wide band of one palm in width, then put two layers of linens over the bandages, and the plaster.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	 Then take a delicate rod three palms in width and length, and wrap it around that bandage, ensuring the head of the bandage hangs down.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	 And place the stake over the break, and turn the bandage around the neck, and below the healthy seat, and below the unhealthy seat.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	 And reset the joints of each part, and when you see that the ligament holds the break again, and it is clearly not moving above the broken bone, reward them every day, and once the bindings are loosened, they heal.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	 And make the sick person lie on their back, and place a small pillow under the seat while they sleep to elevate the shoulder.
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	 If you alleviate the fracture by adjusting the shoulder position or tying the arm to the neck, and no accidental dislocation occurs again until XX days. (XX here is a placeholder for an unspecified number of days)
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	 Then begin the poultice again if it is needed, apply pressure and leave as such until restored.

de la brisure de l’espaule	Regarding a broken shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	 Occasionally the shoulder breaks or moves out of place without a fracture, and it cannot be moved except by touch.
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	 if the apparatus according to the pattern of the break, and resetting in accordance with its natural shape, in all ways that you can.

puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	 then place a wide and fine bandage, slightly wider than the shoulder, and if the edges of the bandage are beyond any part of the shoulder, use a linen gauze to secure it evenly.

de la brisure dou pis	In the breaking of the thighbone
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	 The flesh is never broken in a thousand ways, but this happens rarely;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	 but it often breaks on the other side.

de la brisure des costes	The breaking of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	 Surges that the fracture of ribs only occurs in large ones behind the back and within, and they do not bend easily because they are slick.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	 and feel it well at the inquiry with both hands.

de la brisure dou col	Of the broken rib's bruising
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	 No time there comes a fracture of the hip bone, and rarely does it happen to collapse;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	 And also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	 And when this occurs with anyone, and you need to know if they will be healed or not, take care that if you see their hands become softened, swollen, and lifeless, and cannot move or extend them, and when pricked with a pin, they do not feel it.

et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	 And when it is stabilized on its belly, if there is involuntary defecation.

puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	 Then place on one of the comforting and drying poultices, bind with a bandage, and command the patient to rest.

de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	For the fracture of the hipbone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	 Sometimes the hipbone is fractured, and if so, it has a slight shortening at the top.
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	 And they make a long cut, and descend to the breastbone, and come to pain at the location, and swelling, and break as if broken.

And if the fracture is long or it inclines towards the pelvis, then make the patient lie on his stomach until the restoration of that breakage is aligned properly.

de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of a shoulder joint fracture
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	 Dislocations are those that occur between the shoulder blade and the head of the shoulder, and if they are broken, they must be restored according to one of two ways:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	 One is to take a piece of iron wire long enough in this manner:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	 And make two loops with it, and bend them upwards, then secure the patient on the support.
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	 Then cast the broken arm on the rod so that it reaches the support, and in the middle, make an arch with another rod, then bend it over something heavy or extend the aid towards you.
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	 Then you must set the fracture as if together with its counterpart, until the break is restored as it should be.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that one suspends the patient over his hatter, then ties his hands to his neck, and commands two ministers so that one dyes what is above the break in his hands, and the other dyes below with wool all around it, and stretches each part.
