Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	 And if you see that the extraction is more difficult, then strain at the breakage below and above the breakage, and extend each of the limbs to its place.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	 And if the fracture is near the shoulder blade, it should be bridged by placing one end under the collarbone and the other towards the armpit from the break.
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	 And similarly if the fracture is towards the armpit, you should place the splint gently without much effort, until the break is level with its location and above the collarbone.
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 Then set the fracture as it should be, and splint it, if necessary abscesses do not occur.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	 And if abscesses do occur, do not splint it until seven days have passed, and apply linen soaked in oil of roses for relief, until the abscesses are calmed.
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	 Then you hold it in place, and the method of holding is such that you place the splint over the break, then join the arm over the shoulder, and put your hand on the back or over the chest.
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	 And apply the dressing, and hold it against the shoulder, and along the arm, so that the arm stays straight unless something prevents it or if a bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	 And if you doubt that the bone is not moved, use splints and place one wider and stronger than the others over the fracture, with an interval of space between each splint, so that each splint should be large enough to extend beyond the break by three finger-widths from either side;
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	 Then strain over the fragments as I said at the beginning of the chapter on fractures, more forcefully and less while aligning.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	 And if you see the position of the fragments and alignment, as we have said, during the hour when you restore the broken member, and you doubt the wound is hot, leave it bound until the seventh day, as we have said.
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	 Then check each day for three days that itching or swelling does not occur at the site, or new sores cannot come to the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	 If correctly executed as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	 And if none of these incidents occur, do not discharge the bandage for more than three days or so, and let the patient lie on their back with hands on their abdomen.
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	 And place a bandage made of clean linen evenly on the shoulder, and observe each hour or part of the night, to ensure that the broken limb does not move or the ligaments become softened.
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	 If necessary by the power of medicine, and give him meat that we have previously prescribed, in such a way that the meat is as subtle first.
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	 And when he begins to recover, it becomes larger (or substantial).
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	 And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be restored in forty days altogether.
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	 Then you must dislocate and administer baths and ointment remedies to set it right again.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	 And if the stricture is ugly and twisted, it remains to dislocate for days or months.
de la brisure du bras	Of a fractured arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	 The arm consists of two bones called "phalanges," one small and the other that forms the palm.
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	 And the other is large, and it is he who is outside, toward his small finger.
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	 Perhaps break only the large bone solely, or the small one; and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	 When the small bones are broken, their restoration is easy, and their healing;
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	 And when the large ones are broken, then there is bad healing, and more complicated than if they were both broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	 If it's only small fevers that have been broken, then a little rest is needed and one should be even-keeled.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	 And if it's the large bone, then it must be removed with greater force;
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	 And stretch it over the bone, and lengthen the pocket of the hand higher than the others, and the small fingers lower than the others, and cross them with him immediately, and hold the bone in front of him higher, that the patient may suffer no pain.
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	 Then extend the minister's arm towards the area below its hand or at the elbow, with one assistant on one side and another above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	 Then place the mirror evenly, according to its better form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the break to pieces, place each in its place, and if any are dislocated that they grip their root, and you cannot restore them to their place, then make a cut above and remove the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	 And if there is an injury to the bone, I have discussed this individually with the physician.
si pren la cure.	 then take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	 And if in the beginning there are pus-filled blisters, make a poultice of a cloth soaked with a mixture of rose oil and white wax beeswax, ensuring it is neither too hard nor too soft.
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	 and apply the poultice gently until the pus-filled blisters are soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	 And then remove the poultice and apply a plaster of powdered lime with abundant egg whites. When applying bandages, make them thicker and slightly wider than the others to stay on the fractured area more securely.
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	 And you must understand there are six degrees or different arrangements of arms.
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	 So it is broken in one bone, or two.
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	 And it is held more at the break than elsewhere, and every day less in alignment, as I said at the beginning of this chapter.
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	 And let the dressings be soft and moist over the break, not hard or rough.
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	 And let the bandage used to hold it in place be of flax, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	 And repair the limb and the ligament after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	 And if any accident occurs to the limb, as itching that comes upon the limb, you must bathe the member in warm water until the itch is soothed.
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	 And let the limb rest without any tightness.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	 And then resume the strapping, and if the ligament is softened and the bone displaced, and similar things occur, so shall it be done.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	If care must be taken as the swelling cannot come to the limb because it is too tight, you must soften it slightly and let some days pass until the swelling subsides, then resume straining.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	 And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, then dislocate up until day XX.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	 And between these times, then tie his hands to his neck, and let them be evenly matched, and guard against movement and displacement, and he sleeps on his back.
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	 And know that this fracture is restored in thirty days or fifty, and sometimes in twenty days, according to the composition and temperament of the humors.
de la brisure de la main	Of a fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	It happens that in the palm of the hand and in the knuckles there are few fractures, but rather a bending occurs many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	 And when the plant of the hand is fractured or bent, it requires that the patient sit with their arms crossed evenly before them.
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	 Then place his hand above the extended thigh, and lengthen the broken bones with a straightening force, and align them evenly until they are well joined.
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	 And apply the plaster and dressings, if there is an abscess, then he places a splint according to the amount needed.
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	 And it is wrapped in a cloth of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	 And if there is a break near the ribs around the belly of the sole, make a splint with cloth, and instruct the patient to press it against their broken sole.
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	 and then the strain of a long cloth is applied, and let it be elevated as high as the palm's sole, and held in place as necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the lower part of the limb, it must be placed with a stake underneath and another above on the sole, so that the hand remains open and straight; then wrap it entirely around the wrist, keeping the ligament between the bones taut.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	 And if there is a break on any of our ankles, if it's the malleoli, place them equally as needed.
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	 and strain with the sole, and if you see it then insert a small straight splint to elevate the breakage, and do not move.
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	 If the fracture is of other bones, similarly to those in the index or one of the others, make it even and bind with the healthy bone that follows.
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	 Or you tie them all together tightly so they may move little or no movement, or place a splint underneath as needed.
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	 And take care in the restoration and management of pus-filled abscesses, and remove what arises as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	For the fractured hip
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	 The bone of the hip is often fractured, and it can be seen when it turns forward and backward.
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	 And its repair involves tying ligaments above the breakage, as well as other surrounding areas.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	 The patient lies on their back, then each attendant extends their hand equally to all sides.
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	 And when there is a fracture within the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	 If the fracture is near the root of the hip, then let one ligament go toward the wrist and the other ligament below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	 And also if it's near the knee, then be the ligaments by the knee, and make the extension valgus.
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	 Then place the splint on the bone equal with both hands, so it follows its natural shape, and then apply the cast, and the bandage, if no swelling occurs.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	 And if there is hot swelling, let it be soothed first then return to your work and care.
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	 The ligation is done in the following manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	 It is necessary that you wrap above the fracture with doubled or triple bandages, and leave extra material, then turn the leg until the ankle reaches near the knee's root, and thread a long string between the thigh and leg, below the knee, let the top part of the cord hang over.
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	 Then turn to the leg and thigh, bandage them, then apply a dressing over any wounds, and place an iron bar on the leg bone.
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	 Then wrap the space between the leg and thigh with soft cloth to ensure even pressure, then begin binding using three or four turns around the wound.
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	 And as you increase above the wound, decrease the tightness.
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	 Then take two more strands of thread that you have tied between the leg and thigh, and bind three dressings on top of them, then return to untie at the head end of the thread as far as reaching the foot.
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	 If it does not move back to its place, leave it like that, then ensure no abscess or swelling occurs again.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	 And if it occurs, when resetting is done, and directed as described, as we have said many times.
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	 And if there are broken bone fragments that catch, the repositioning may be required if possible.
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	 and if it cannot be done, then incision of the limb must be made, and ligaments severed.
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	 and the treatment is as we have said until it is sound again.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	 And never should the thigh be broken as such when placed in splints, like in shoulders and arms.
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	 Nevertheless, in this kind of restoration done, it does not harm the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored within a day or so, depending on the variations of constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	From the hollow of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	 Know that in the groove of the neck there is often a slight fracture, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	 And if it breaks, it is not so much a crack, but a split or piercing, and leads to any wound, feels of the wound, and this smells quite foul.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	 And if there is restoration by setting equally what was separated at its joints, so that it can be moved and healed.
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	 Then place the splint, and put a round peg if needed, and restrain it as necessary, then address all other issues we have mentioned regarding fractures, like abscesses that burn and similar matters.
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Do what is appropriate for each injury so that it heals properly.
de la brisure de la jambe	On the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	 Know that in the leg there are two bones, one called "tibia" and the other called "femur".
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	 and there are all types of fractures as they occur in the arm, and therefore the treatment is like that for the arm equally, and the procedures are all there. And if both bones are broken together, turn the leg from all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, turn it forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	 And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it can be seen clearly.
et torne desoz.	 Yet then turn away from it.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	 Then prepare for stretching, align properly, and secure the ligaments evenly.
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	 but nonetheless, if it is an unsightly breakage with some fragments present, then the stretching should be minor and lighter.
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	 and keep upright according to your virtue (strength).
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	 And when you have completed your work, take the weighted wooden staves that extend along the leg from knee to ankle on both sides.
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	 then wrap them with two strips of cloth above and below, securely tying the middle so that the leg cannot bend to either side, thus it is well.
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	 And no one administers oil to the length of the leg, and it heals as wood, and places the leg in position to prevent movement, and properly treats the break where there is injury.
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	 And each day moves the leg, to check if there are any abscesses or other accidents.
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it heals until it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	On the breakage of bone in the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but at the bone of the foot it comes to a fracture and the bones are slightly dislocated, with no injury occurring in some other conditions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	 And if it occurs as a broken bone in the foot, and you see the bones protruding on top of each other, place such malaise limbs flat on the ground as if they were to walk, then now put your leg under theirs where the bones are elevated, and press until they return to their places.
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	 Then place the poultice and apply pressure thereon, then take a small tablet at II inches from the navel, then strain it back in position immediately, then wrap with bandages around, and other things of which you are in need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, you may loosen the bandage, for you will find the bones to be equal again, whether fractured or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	 And if any nerves are broken, restore them as we have described for the hand's nerves.
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	 then place an iron bar of the same length as the nerve, and make it slightly wider, then take that tablet from under the hip as I mentioned, and strain back immediately.
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	 and if there are two or three, or more broken, place under each a bar according to its quantity, wrapped in one cloth of flax, and strain the tablet from under the hip.
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	 And it is when on top of the shoulder blade lies the belly with a feverish pain, so that one may grasp firmly.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	 And it is necessary not to forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, which we have mentioned;
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	 and treat each injury as it ought to be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	For a fracture of the bone of the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	 When the bone of womanly nature is broken, and she should sit in a chair expanded, then incline it to the part of her back that hurts, and be held from behind;
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	 then fill the maiden's body with cotton cloth, placing as much as it can hold.
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	 then stand the woman up, and lift her back little by little, and thus remove the cotton when it comes to the entrance of her body, returning the bone with its natural position.
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	 And when she wishes to urinate, provide her with a sponge, and once she has urinated, reset it, thus doing so for seven days or more.
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	 If this is restored, and if you see it, take a sheepskin bladder, tie its neck with thread, and fill the entire bladder with water from the stream.
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	 Then blow into the bladder until it is fully inflated.
la nature si revenra li brisure;	 The body will return to restore the fracture;
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then it should be filled with cotton and left that way for several days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	 And when the bone of the arm or woman's limb is broken as we have described in the thigh bone.
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 And these fractures are not hidden from those who devote themselves to its study and application; listen to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	 For a fracture indicates various conditions affecting the proper path of restoration:
enten le donques.	 So understand this.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	 In the phallus, when it is broken, takes on a goose's neck and inserts itself.
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	 Then wrap dressings around it, and leave them there for three days or more, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for those with fractures and wounds, especially if they are large like the bone of the hip or shoulder or similar, that they be healed now so that the signs we have mentioned testify to them.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healed and there are no foreign bodies present, then again begin to restore the fracture in the same hour or day, unless an abscess develops.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	When abscesses occur there, allow the healing until the third day, as long as the abscess is calmed, and do not touch or disturb it either on the second or fourth day, for you would bring about a harmful incident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible at its location, it must be carefully set with slight pressure from your hands in small extensions.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	 And if the extension does not fit to make both hands equal, then use this instrument made of iron with seven or eight long pieces, and its width is according to the amount of the wound.
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	 and so it requires three or four fingers from the barber to grasp, depending on how much is needed for each treatment of fractures.
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	 and it should be slightly long and somewhat thicker, so that it does not bend under pressure on the limb during your work, and have an edge in front, and thickness towards the middle like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	 And it is called "palisandre," so that the arching of the neck must be placed on the visible part of the bone.
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 And you must touch it once so that it returns, and they are equal to each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 And if the fractures are subtle, and the tissues cannot properly take hold of the bone, then you must cut off the visible part of the baboon until the tissues have opportunity.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	 And if you cannot bring back the bone, as we have said, use a suitable instrument for this, either an incision or a saw, to your ability.
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	 then retrieve what is lodged in the hard bone with sharpness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is returned to its place, and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	 If you manage to place it back where it belongs, then anoint the wound with vinegar and black sticking tonic properly if so.
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	 and do not put any cerate or other substance on the wound that contains oil, lest it causes decay and infection.
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	 then apply bandages as you have restored the bebone, and leave the wound uncovered, covering it entirely with a dressing according to the amount of the wound, ensuring that the injury is not strained with the fracture.
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	 And many times have they done this foolish physician, bringing forth from the patient who is dead or corrupted at some point.
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 And let it be that he makes the fracture more gentle and softer than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	 And if the wound is severe or large, and you doubt that some unforeseen event may occur, as we have said, and there is pain at the site, then it does not require setting with splints.
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 but wrap around it, in place of splints, use sturdy cloths and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And when after one or two days you see infection at the wound, take whatever you have applied and add healing salve to it, as with Tetrapharmacist's ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	It is necessary to loosen the limb two times a day, morning and evening, until it becomes loose and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limb should be set in such a way that the bow bends gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	If more than one day passes and it cannot be joined but returns with pain, because there are small pieces of bone in the way, then you must carefully cleanse the wound and remove all those displaced fragments that cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 And if a fistula comes at the site or another form of decay occurs, it must be treated as described in this chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	 And when the bone is broken and visible above the limb, as with the hip or shoulder bones, and other similar large body parts, do not treat it, for many times death comes, but let it remain until it heals.
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	 By chance it may heal itself after XX days or XXX, then treat the wound, if you know how.
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 and if you do not know, leave it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	Of bruises that appear around the sore
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	 We often come to heal the break after bone health, especially when it is near the joint, and there is an unsightly appearance of the limb.
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	 and sometimes it cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	 Therefore be cautious if we are weakened:
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	 if you administer medicines like aloes, incense, and myrrh, along with acacia and other similar substances, whether you use any of these individually or all together, mix them with astringent wine or an abundance of honey or oil.
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	 And place them on the knives for cutting, and hold firmly without loosening hands.
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	 Then dislocate it, and do another one, as long as necessary movements occur.
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	 or strain a well-made lump of flesh;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	 because the properties of this flesh are such that it pulls out all inflammations from over the limbs.
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	 and if the movement is already converted into hardness just like a stone, and there is a need to remove it, so remove excess flesh.
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 or reshape by any razor until it is removed, and heal as long as it is cleaned up.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The member that is weak after recovery
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	 When the broken bone is restored, and after follows weak and subtle limbs for many reasons:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	 Because one was made too tightly, and it was not loosened as it should be.
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	 Or because there were too many bindings, preventing the member from regaining its normal size.
ou por multitude d’arosement;	 Or due to excessive rubbing.
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	 Or by making movements that are too large and not at the right time.
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	 Or because it has little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	 And the treatment should be that you feed the patient well and make the body supple until there is an increase in blood.
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	 And provide him with a bath, and give him joy and ease.
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	 Then apply poultices to the limb such that they draw much swelling away from it and often change with water, until the swelling subsides in the limb.
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	 And returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The twisted member after health is restored
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	 When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the bones are broken openly, and the shape of the limb is ugly, however, it does not lose its natural function.
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	 if you do not believe the simpletons who say that one must break the limb anew entirely, and many foolish men have done this in our land.
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	 and such actions are condemned, which brings great harm, and sometimes death.
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	 however, if the knots and twists are recent, it is appropriate that they be loosened with warm water, or soft herbs boiled like valerian leaves, roots, and milk thistle, among similar things.
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	 And the poultice softening agent you take as Aquilon properly made, and you collect the mucilage of wormwood, and mix it with fat of geese or oil of sesame, and make a poultice on top.
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	 Or you take soothing fats, and grind them with columbine seed, and certain medicines that alleviate the tightness.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 At no time is bone broken by rubbing continuously and lengthily with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 And so provide relief to the movement of each limb at every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	 And if the tortuousness is old and hardened, just like stone, and it needs to be removed by iron, then if necessary, use the saw-like instrument gently up to the bone.
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	 And apply cuisson and continue with treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint is out of its place, so it cannot move, and the limb is misaligned, causing great pain and injury to the patient.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When any dislocation occurs, now you must return it without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	 Because if one is late, the swelling increases, and perhaps when resetting it causes pain at its place.
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	 For this reason, it is not advisable to move it when it has swelled.
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	 Many times brings forth pain and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	 Nevertheless, when this occurs, make the patient take wine, then leave them alone until the swelling is calmed.
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 Then raise the limb with warm water and oil, then gently flex it, and treat each member as care comes to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters on shoulder joint dislocations up to fractures.
des mandibules	Of lower jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	 Sometimes the jawbones are dislocated inwardly, and there are two ways of dislocation for both sides.
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	 or they are a little out of their place, and become slightly softened;
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	 or they are dislocated entirely, hanging towards the left, and causing saliva from the mouth that cannot be held, not able to close its mouth, and wrapping around the tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns through various positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	 If it is complete and accomplished, one must promptly reset it without delay.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	 In such a way that the minister dyes your head with the patient's hand and inserts the mirror slightly into one of its roots at the location of the lower jaw's dislocation inside the mouth; if the dislocation is on both sides.
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	 And let the other two hands be far enough to place them evenly.
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 Then instruct the patient to soften his jawbones and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	The mirror is placed to make it level, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	 And if resetting is difficult, especially when both jawbones are together, apply hot water and oil until they can be gently adjusted.
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	 Do not attempt to move it back as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	 And when they are returned evenly, and the wound of the patient heals well and becomes softened, then place a cloth soaked in a mixture made of rose oil and wax on it, and lightly bind it with thin threads.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	 the patient should sleep on his back with his head between two pillows, and not move to either side or make any effort to turn over, but gently eat tender meat until the pains are gone, and the jaws have healed.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 and then offer him what he wishes to eat lightly, and not strain to open his mouth while eating or drinking until the jaw is fully healed and healthy.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	If the two lower jaws cannot be put back in place within an hour and are not restored to their original positions, fever and usual sweats may occur, and possibly intestinal obstruction, and perhaps they vomit clear fluid.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	 And when you see this, then you know it is dislocation.
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	 and many times the one who suffers from it can die within 9 days.
de la forcelle	of the sinew.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The strong bone cannot be dislocated from within the ribs and at the end of the shinbone, and it is not dislocated even once by accident, but one feels it keenly.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	 And the restoration is such that the patient lies on their back and extends their arms;
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	 then you press the joint firmly with your palm, and it will return.
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	 then place on the splint and apply the bandage, securing it.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	 and the one lying towards the edge cannot dislocate;
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	 if not, and if it ever does dislocate again, reset it to its place as we have said.
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	 then apply the splint and bandage, secure it, and advise the patient to rest until they are well again.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 And thus bring back the head of the shoulder blade when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	 Sections that the shoulder can be dislocated in three ways:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	 One is because it dislocates from the lower part of the shoulder to above.
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	 and the second is at the upper part.
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	 And sometimes dislocates to the upper part, but this happens little.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	 and does not dislocate backward for the shoulder, nor does it dislocate inward for the nerves;
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	 and often dislocates upward toward the collarbone, especially in those with little strength, for these it moves very quickly.
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 to those with enough strength, it goes with ease and reenters easily.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And occasionally some men may experience blows or fractures, and their shoulder swells with intense heat, believing it to be dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	 Thus one must try it, as long as you are certain;
et adonques encomence la cure.	 and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	 And is known when dislocation occurs toward the collarbone, and there is a difference between the affected shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find their marked diversity;
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	 And you will find at the head of the shoulder a pit, and underneath the socket where the top of the shoulder meets, just as if it were some eggs.
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	 And the patient cannot bring their hand back to its place, nor make any movements at all;
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	 And similarly, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you can clearly see the socket.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 This way of dislocation cannot be corrected if it is new, or when the child becomes ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	 And the method is for the minister to raise the patient's hand upward, then put pebbles underne cuff, and lift the joint with great strength at its place.
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	 And the minister takes hold of the hand, extends it upward, then places it below.
si venra hastanment.	 If done swiftly and skillfully.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	 And if it does not occur as we have said on the following day, it is necessary for the patient to be bathed in warm water.
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	 and treat gently with soothing substances such as an infusion of wormwood, fennel, and honey in water, and be treated.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	 then rest the patient on their back, and place under the buttocks a strip of linen that is neither too soft nor too hard, then position the ankle bone on top of the strip, and carefully elevate the head of the shoulder, and treat the hand gently.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	 And other remedies apply to the patient's head so it does not move forward.
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	 and if that shoulder returns immediately, then examine whether you reset according to this method:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	 And ensure that there is a person who is larger than the patient.
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	 And stand directly to their side, and lift the shoulder from under the seat of the patient, raising the seat upward so that the patient hangs in the air.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 And other remedeus guide the patient's hand towards their belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too light, reinforce with them something heavy, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	 And reset in another manner:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	 And it is that you insert a long stick into the ground so that the head is aligned as with an axis, and not too thick nor too narrow.
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	 Then it is put under the patient, but with soft cloths above, and the patient lies long on their back.
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	 Then the hand should be extended downwards to the other side gently, and the joint will return to its place quickly.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	 And if it does not want to return for all these reasons that we have mentioned, then do this treatment:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 Take an iron stick of length five and two inches in width, which has the head bent to enter into the elbow from above, as follows:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	 Then put soft cloths over the back of the patient, so that the elbow does not scratch the patient, then place it under the joint of the affected limb.
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	 Extend the other arm over the length of the back, and place the shoulder over it, then extend the head of the hand, and put the arm under the slot of a stool with wide arms, and let the hands hang downwards on the opposite side.
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	 The joint may now remain fixed.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, no matter how, you must put a woolen thread beneath the shoulder, then apply an ointment cloth of powder from grinding, with incense and myrrh oil on all around the shoulder, then quickly strain undernehemenent, and turn the linen over the ointment, wrapping it around its collar, and let the hands hang in this manner.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	 And it is necessary that he rests a little, until the limb is comforted, for it will heal sooner.
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	 and then rest more after 3 or 7 days, and move [it].
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	 and if it is firm and not softened, it will be healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the dislocation is severe due to the moisture that has occurred or another reason, it must be tended with three small fire cauteries as mentioned in the treatise of fire cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	 And if you do all this, and it dislocates again after nine days, and the joint does not stay in place, nor can lift either arm upwards; then know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder are pinched or stretched or softened.
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	 and understand that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	 The dislocation that occurs towards the lower part and scapulae, or backward, is caused by impact, extension of the hands, and other measures are taken.
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And treat until it is whole again.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after healing comes weakness in the limb and delays in movement, causing the patient great pain many times until the stiffness is alleviated, and it returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	Of the dislocation of the shoulder blade
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	 Know that the shoulder joint has dislocated from its place and returns to points;
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	 And it is dislocated in all parts, mainly at the front and back, and the dislocation cannot be reduced, as one can clearly see and feel it.
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	 and dislocates according to each position.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when you join the maligned limb with its proper alignment, if it can be seen clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 Because the dislocation is raised, and cannot bend the arm or reach its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	 And it is necessary for you to reset it as soon as a bone protrudes because if the bone were to emerge, it would be difficult to realign.
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	 and perhaps cannot always be realigned completely, especially when it is at the back;
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	 it's worse than other dislocations, and causes more pain, and perhaps there may be death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	 And restoration is when it can be returned to such extent that you spread its hand with your two hands.
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	 and its arms are spread wide, and the hands turn as follows throughout it, above and below, positioning the joint with all of its fingers together or at the root of its palm, until they return to their place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, when it comes back after doubling its hand with its own hand and fixing the root of the palm that has been dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	 And if it does not want to go back to its place, give a strong stretching.
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	 and there are two ministers who extend the arm, and they hold it with both hands, so that it does not move during stretching.
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	 then turn the arm from each side, after you have wrapped a long and wide double cloth around it.
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	 When the muscle attaches to the joint near its hand, if you anoint it with any oil to soften the joint, then rejoin the joint properly until it heals.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 And when it is in place, if you securely wrap with linen bandages and strain gently, then support the arm at the ache-ridden joint, leave it for several days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	 And if the joint is firm in place, you may loosen the ligaments and let them be.
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	 And if you see that the joint does not tighten well, start anew with bandaging and ligaments, leave them for several days until they are firmly in place.
puis le deslie.	 Then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	 And if it feels stiffness after the joint's resetting and moves, then bathe well and rub gently, pressing until relieved.
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	 Or place a fat sheep's grease on the joint, then leave it for a day and a night, then bandage, and let them take their bath.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	 And when they sweat, rub the joint promptly, then reapply the fat, and then take a bath.
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And do this two or three times until healed.
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	 And if you see swelling, apply warm damp fenugreek paste mixed with butter and bind it.
si revenra a sa disposition.	 If it returns to normal condition.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	 The hand's joint dislocates easily, and its return is lighter than other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	 Nevertheless, it must be brought back to its place promptly, at the same time as it is dislocated, so that the joint can swell or an abscess may arise there.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	 And the adjustments are such that you place your hand over a table, extend your fingers, and align them evenly, so that you put your palm on the joint's surface, and press until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	 Nevertheless, it is necessary to check if it is properly in place.
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 Then the patient should put their back on their hand over a table during extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 If the dislocation is in the back of the hand, place the patient's hand on a tabletop and mirror position your hand over that joint appearance.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	 If it returns now, that is well.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If not, and the strain from soothing balms causes an abscess, then let it be as such to begin again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	 And if it cannot bear being left off, and you are unable to place it back after any days, the twisted joint will persist.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	 nor can anything be done for the patient until their hand has become softened and cannot grasp or extract any objects at all.
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	 then you know that the nerves are cut or the artery is affected.
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 if there is no other remedy but to extract through surgery near the wound, and perhaps it brings no further benefit.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hands are placed correctly, place them on the plaque we have mentioned, then grasp it and leave for 5 days, then release and keep like this.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot move well, and there is no loosening, then apply warm water to the area, and rub until it becomes smooth.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Of dislocating the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	 Never are either of the bones of the hand dislocated to any side, neither towards the back of the palm nor its underside.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	 Then they are to be tied up and the dislocation is put back into place until it stays, then support the head of the shoulder, and bend towards the part where it was dislocated.
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	 And leave it for two days, then on the third day make it equal again.
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	 and from this nourish him as we have said, leave him for a day, then make him move again, and reconnect the nourishment.
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 and do this often until it is narrow again, just the same, if it is dislocated on the palm of the hand, then proceed as you did before, until it becomes healthy.
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 And do likewise when it is dislocated elsewhere.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Double dislocation of the spine or backbone.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine of the back or neck is dislocated, if there are several occurring, there is no remedy, as it hastens death for the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	 And the signs are that the urination gushes out without volition, cannot be held in, and many times some limb is weakened, either both hips or one arm or leg.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	 And many times the spine dislocates four parts.
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	 The one that moves at the back is called "gilborsis":
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	 This treatment is for when you find "gilborsis" resulting from childhood.
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 If there's no remedy or healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	 And the one that comes from falling or blows or similar things, according to old methods of treatment by using many words, it does not have much benefit in all.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 But I've abbreviated according to my intention and formed remedies in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	 I say that in the "gilborsis" occurring at the front of the thighs, there is no cure or health.
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	 And similarly those that come directly to both sides, and cannot be healed except for the one properly coming onto the back, as I say.
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	 And that the patient be stretched equally across his face in one place, and have support from below him, so he does not fall.
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	 Then stick a splint to the head in earth firmly, and one at the feet, and tie a bandage around the limbs of the patient, and another on the hips, knees, ankles.
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	 And two ministers know the bindings, one to the head and the other to the feet, among the two splints.
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 And they should be securely closed, as we have said about the splint, and the healer place his palms firmly on the spine, until it recovers.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	 If it does not return with this treatment, take a stick three arms long, and chevron from the front, position the patient on their side, then place the head of the stick under the forehead, and then set the middle of the stick against the spine.
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	 And place the ends of their feet under the other end of the stick and press firmly until it returns to its place.
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 And if you see that twists toward the elbow, apply pressure with your hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	 And take two sticks of great length to the head of the patient's arm and toward the other two fingers, placing between each stick an ample space in width.
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	 And have on each stick one knot where it bends correctly, and the sticks should be firmly in place so that they do not move.
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	 And among these burners should there be one burning piece returning to where the ribbons return, and have in it two smaller pieces of the width of a palm, for turning the wheel.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 And then attach the ribbons that are among the cables to the wheel's axis and the other ribbons to the pieces on the opposite wheel, with each servant turning their respective wheels throughout the entire length of the ribbon, and the master ensures the spine is aligned as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And when it is aligned, place on an embalming desiccant with plenty of ointment, then the plugs, and then the splint from a tablet three fingers wide to properly fix the fracture site and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with ribbons as we have said, and apply subtle nourishment to the patient until they are well.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	 And if any issue arises at the end of health recovery, it is necessary to administer soothing and calming medicines, with the spoon that we have mentioned here before.
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	 And never administer a piece of metal or iron, and when the appearance appears in the lower part of the back, believe that it is dislocation.
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	 And it is the bone that opens up, so there should be no assumption about it:
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	 Perhaps death could come as a result.
des dislocations de la hainche	Des dislocations du genou
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	 I say that the hip and shoulder joints only come from dislocation alone, not like other joints.
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	 And the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parts:
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	 Outward and inward, front and back;
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	 And further inside and out thereof, with it dislocated forward and backward.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	 And the recognition of its dislocation inwardly is such that when joining the affected limb with the healthy one, it is longer and opens more joints on the diseased side than the healthy, so the afflicted cannot double their knuckles over fire.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 And it is the sinew which is near an inflamed abscess, because the head of the hip comes close to it.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	The sign of it occurring to one is that this accident is contrary to those before.
